###begin article-title 0
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 106 128 106 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis elegans</italic>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 106 128 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
Pseudomonas aeruginosa Suppresses Host Immunity by Activating the DAF-2 Insulin-Like Signaling Pathway in Caenorhabditis elegans
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Conceived and designed the experiments: EAE TK MWT. Performed the experiments: EAE TK MWT. Analyzed the data: EAE TK MWT. Wrote the paper: EAE TK MWT.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 201 223 201 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 314 336 314 336 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis elegans</italic>
###xml 645 658 645 658 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 919 932 919 932 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1263 1268 1263 1268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1270 1275 1270 1275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1281 1286 1281 1286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1300 1313 1300 1313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1443 1465 1443 1465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Salmonella typhimurium</italic>
###xml 1469 1490 1469 1490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Enterococcus faecalis</italic>
###xml 1536 1549 1536 1549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 201 223 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 314 336 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
###xml 645 658 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 919 932 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1300 1313 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1443 1465 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">Salmonella typhimurium</span>
###xml 1469 1490 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">Enterococcus faecalis</span>
###xml 1536 1549 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Some pathogens have evolved mechanisms to overcome host immune defenses by inhibiting host defense signaling pathways and suppressing the expression of host defense effectors. We present evidence that Pseudomonas aeruginosa is able to suppress the expression of a subset of immune defense genes in the animal host Caenorhabditis elegans by activating the DAF-2/DAF-16 insulin-like signaling pathway. The DAF-2/DAF-16 pathway is important for the regulation of many aspects of organismal physiology, including metabolism, stress response, longevity, and immune function. We show that intestinal expression of DAF-16 is required for resistance to P. aeruginosa and that the suppression of immune defense genes is dependent on the insulin-like receptor DAF-2 and the FOXO transcription factor DAF-16. By visualizing the subcellular localization of DAF-16::GFP fusion protein in live animals during infection, we show that P. aeruginosa-mediated downregulation of a subset of immune genes is associated with the ability to translocate DAF-16 from the nuclei of intestinal cells. Suppression of DAF-16 is mediated by an insulin-like peptide, INS-7, which functions upstream of DAF-2. Both the inhibition of DAF-16 and downregulation of DAF-16-regulated genes, such as thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1, require the P. aeruginosa two-component response regulator GacA and the quorum-sensing regulators LasR and RhlR and are not observed during infection with Salmonella typhimurium or Enterococcus faecalis. Our results reveal a new mechanism by which P. aeruginosa suppresses host immune defense.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Author Summary
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 462 484 462 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 663 685 663 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis elegans</italic>
###xml 851 864 851 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1110 1123 1110 1123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1291 1304 1291 1304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 462 484 <span type="species:ncbi:287">Pseudomonas aeruginosa</span>
###xml 663 685 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
###xml 851 864 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1110 1123 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1291 1304 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1363 1368 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Bacterial pathogens have evolved mechanisms to overcome the immune defenses that animals and plants deploy against them. In some cases, this involves directly interfering with the proper functioning of the immune system. Because pathogens that employ these strategies are often the most deadly and difficult to treat, it is important to understand how they are able to suppress the immune system in the context of the whole organism. In this paper, we show that Pseudomonas aeruginosa, a bacterial pathogen that is a major contributor to hospital-borne infections such as pneumonia, suppresses an immune defense pathway during infection of the simple animal host Caenorhabditis elegans. Using genetic modifications of both the pathogen and host, we identify components of the signaling pathways required to suppress host immune defenses. We find that P. aeruginosa employs the cell-to-cell communication system known as quorum sensing, which coordinates the expression of virulence factors to suppress host immune defense. In the host, an evolutionarily conserved insulin-like signaling pathway is affected by P. aeruginosa, resulting in the suppression of genes that are required for defense against infection in the intestinal epithelial cells. These findings suggest the possibility that P. aeruginosa may exploit similar mechanisms when causing infections of human epithelium, such as the epithelial lining of the lungs.
###end p 4

###xml 1321 1325 1313 1317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Mallo1">[10]</xref>
###xml 1394 1404 1386 1396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1545 1555 1537 1547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1689 1693 1678 1682 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Ewbank1">[11]</xref>

###xml 1769 1774 1758 1763 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pmk-1</italic>
###xml 1850 1854 1839 1843 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kim1">[13]</xref>
###xml 1867 1872 1856 1861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6</italic>
###xml 1962 1966 1948 1952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Mallo1">[10]</xref>
###xml 1967 1971 1953 1957 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Tan1">[14]</xref>
###xml 1997 2002 1983 1988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 2111 2116 2097 2102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 2188 2192 2174 2178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Garsin1">[15]</xref>
###xml 2392 2395 2378 2381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 2396 2400 2382 2386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Murphy1">[16]</xref>
###xml 2401 2405 2387 2391 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Mochii1">[17]</xref>
###xml 315 325 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 330 340 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 989 999 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 1229 1239 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1394 1404 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1545 1555 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The innate immune system is a genetically-encoded host defense mechanism that constitutes the first line of defense against pathogens in plants and animals. Innate immunity in animals is evolutionarily ancient, and the molecular components of mammalian innate immunity are partly conserved in invertebrates such as Drosophila and C. elegans that lack a somatic recombination-based adaptive immunity. Innate immunity comprises several functions, including the production of defense proteins, such as antimicrobial peptides, lysozymes, and other immune modulators [1]. A common theme emerging from the studies of host-pathogen interactions is that recognition of pathogen-associated molecular patterns (PAMPs) or of infection byproducts by host receptors, such as the Toll-like receptors (TLRs), trigger highly regulated immune responses, including the induction of antimicrobial effectors [2],[3]. For example, infection by Gram-positive bacteria triggers activation of the Toll pathway in Drosophila. Activation of Toll signaling in turn induces expression of specific antimicrobial genes through the activation of a Rel/NF-kappaB transcription factor [4],[5]. Despite lacking a functionally conserved TLR/NF-kappaB pathway [6], C. elegans is able to mount robust immune responses against a variety of pathogens (see [7]-[10] for examples). This underscores the importance of other pathways in C. elegans innate immunity. Recently, through genetic studies, several conserved signal transduction pathways that are required for innate immunity in C. elegans have been identified. They include the p38 MAPK, the Sma/TGF-beta, and the DAF-2/DAF-16 insulin-like signaling pathways (reviewed in [11],[12]). For example, mutants in sek-1, which encodes a p38 MAPK kinase, and pmk-1, which encodes a p38 MAPK, are sensitive to killing by bacterial pathogens [13]. Mutants in sma-6, which encodes a TGF-beta receptor, are also sensitive to killing by bacterial pathogens [10],[14]. In contrast, mutants in daf-2, which encodes an insulin-like receptor, are resistant to killing by bacterial pathogens. The resistance of daf-2 mutants is completely dependent on DAF-16, a FOXO transcription factor [15]. Microarray studies suggest that each of these immune signaling pathways regulates the expression of host effector genes, which may account for the altered pathogen susceptibility of pathway mutants [8],[16],[17].
###end p 6

###xml 319 323 319 323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Mallo1">[10]</xref>

###xml 594 599 594 599 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abf-2</italic>
###xml 616 626 616 626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 793 797 793 797 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kato1">[18]</xref>
###xml 798 802 798 802 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Banyai1">[19]</xref>
###xml 870 880 870 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 880 884 880 884 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Alegado1">[20]</xref>
###xml 890 900 890 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 984 989 984 989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-1</italic>
###xml 993 998 993 998 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-8</italic>
###xml 1031 1041 1031 1041 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1097 1100 1097 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn</italic>
###xml 1169 1182 1169 1182 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1182 1185 1182 1185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1256 1266 1256 1266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1266 1269 1266 1269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1270 1274 1270 1274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Mallo1">[10]</xref>
###xml 1375 1379 1375 1379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wong1">[21]</xref>
###xml 1628 1632 1628 1632 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Couillault1">[22]</xref>
###xml 1899 1902 1899 1902 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 1903 1907 1903 1907 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kerry1">[23]</xref>
###xml 183 193 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 329 339 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 548 560 <span type="species:ncbi:6253">Ascaris suum</span>
###xml 616 626 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 870 880 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 890 900 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1031 1041 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1169 1182 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1256 1266 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Host defense effectors include diverse classes of small molecules and antimicrobial peptides. Lysozyme, a bacteriolytic enzyme, is ubiquitously expressed in mammalian secretions. The C. elegans genome encodes ten lysozyme-like proteins (lys-1 to lys-10), some of which have been directly implicated in host defense [7],[10]. The C. elegans genome also encodes many amoebapore or saposin-like proteins (e.g., spp-1) that are members of a large and diverse class of antimicrobial peptides and a number of defensin-like molecules homologous to ASABF (Ascaris suum antibacterial factor), including abf-2. In mammals and Drosophila, the expression of defensin-family proteins contributes to antibacterial, antifungal, and antiviral defenses. Recombinant SPP-1 and ABF-2 have antimicrobial activity [18],[19], and endogenous expression contributes to antibacterial defense in C. elegans[20]. The C. elegans genome also encodes homologs of the thaumatin family of plant antifungal proteins (thn-1 to thn-8). While it is not known whether C. elegans thaumatins have antifungal activity, RNAi knockdown of thn-family genes results in worms that are more sensitive to killing by P. aeruginosa[7]. Host effector genes are differentially regulated during infection of C. elegans[7]-[10]. Microarray studies also suggest that different pathogens elicit specific transcriptional responses [21]. This is presumably due to host recognition of different PAMPs followed by induction of specific host defense pathways. For example, during fungal infection, TIR-1 (Toll and IL-1 receptor) activates an antifungal defense through p38 MAPK signaling [22]. The mechanisms by which specific transcriptional responses are elicited are still largely unknown. However, the intestine-specific GATA transcription factor ELT-2 is required for the regulation of host immune defense effectors and resistance to bacterial pathogens [7],[23].
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 0 13 0 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 123 127 123 127 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wood1">[24]</xref>
###xml 202 206 202 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Saiman1">[25]</xref>
###xml 207 211 207 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lyczak1">[26]</xref>
###xml 213 214 213 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P</italic>
###xml 216 226 216 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 320 333 320 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 570 574 570 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 620 624 620 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 629 633 629 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 633 637 633 637 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Reimmann1">[27]</xref>
###xml 638 642 638 642 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Rahme1">[28]</xref>
###xml 657 670 657 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 720 724 720 724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Turner1">[29]</xref>
###xml 832 836 832 836 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lau1">[30]</xref>
###xml 846 859 846 859 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1208 1212 1208 1212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Gross1">[31]</xref>
###xml 1248 1261 1248 1261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1399 1403 1399 1403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Hong1">[32]</xref>
###xml 1404 1408 1404 1408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Schmidtchen1">[33]</xref>
###xml 1768 1781 1764 1777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1870 1874 1866 1870 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wolfgang1">[34]</xref>
###xml 1875 1879 1871 1875 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Palmer1">[35]</xref>
###xml 2009 2022 2005 2018 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 2039 2049 2035 2045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 2222 2226 2218 2222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Apidianakis1">[36]</xref>
###xml 0 13 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 44 49 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 114 122 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 160 168 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 213 226 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 320 333 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 657 670 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 846 859 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1248 1261 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1758 1766 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 1768 1781 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 2009 2022 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 2039 2049 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
P. aeruginosa is an important Gram-negative human pathogen that is associated with infection of immunocompromised patients [24], including cystic fibrosis (CF) patients and individuals with burn wounds [25],[26]. P. aeruginosa has evolved at least three strategies to combat the vast repertoire of host defenses. First, P. aeruginosa can produce an extensive array of cell-associated and secreted virulence factors that are deleterious or damaging to the host. A substantial number of these virulence determinants are regulated by the two-component regulator encoded by gacA and the quorum-sensing regulators encoded by lasR and rhlR[27],[28]. For example, P. aeruginosa secretes several phenazines, including pyocyanin [29], that have tissue-damaging properties attributed to the induction of free radical production in host cells [30]. Second, P. aeruginosa can evade detection by the host, either by directly destroying host molecules that are involved in pathogen detection or by downregulating PAMP expression. For example, an important component of host defense is the deposition of a complement component C3b on the bacterial surface, leading to the induction of host responses and pathogen clearance [31]. To counter complement activation, P. aeruginosa produces alginate to limit accessibility of complement and secretes proteases, including alkaline protease and elastase that degrade C3b [32],[33]. The flagellum, an important virulence determinant required for motility and attachment, is also a PAMP that is detected by the host through the interaction of monomeric flagellin with TLR5, resulting in NF-kappaB and p38 MAPK activation; this innate immune response is intended to protect the host. Upon growth on purulent mucus from CF and non-CF patients, P. aeruginosa downregulates flagellin synthesis, thereby blunting the host protective immune response [34],[35]. A third strategy is to compromise the host by suppressing the host defense responses. It has been suggested that the ability of P. aeruginosa to rapidly kill Drosophila is associated with downregulation of antimicrobial peptide expression by a yet-unknown mechanism that requires a putative S-adenosyl-methionine-dependent methyltransfrease [36].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 71 84 71 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 164 167 164 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 168 172 168 172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Pauli1">[37]</xref>
###xml 245 257 245 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2, spp-1</italic>
###xml 263 268 263 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 314 327 314 327 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 473 486 473 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 500 510 500 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 544 557 544 557 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 923 936 923 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1044 1057 1044 1057 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1071 1081 1071 1081 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 71 84 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 314 327 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 473 486 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 500 510 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 544 557 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 923 936 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1044 1057 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1071 1081 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
We found that an unexpected feature of the transcriptional response to P. aeruginosa is the downregulation of several intestinally-expressed host defense effectors [7],[37]. We hypothesized that repression of immune effector expression, such as thn-2, spp-1, and lys-7, may represent a virulence mechanism used by P. aeruginosa to suppress host defenses. In this report, we identify both host and pathogen factors required for the downregulation of immune effectors during P. aeruginosa infection of C. elegans. We present data indicating that P. aeruginosa infection causes the activation of DAF-2 insulin-like signaling, which leads to translocation of DAF-16 protein from nuclei of intestinal cells and downregulation of DAF-16 transcriptional targets. Delocalization of DAF-16 requires DAF-2 and an upstream neuroendocrine signaling pathway, including the DAF-2 agonist INS-7. Each of these effects is dependent on the P. aeruginosa two-component regulator GacA and the quorum-sensing regulators LasR and RhlR. Our results demonstrate that P. aeruginosa infection of C. elegans results in the suppression of intestinal immune defense through virulence factor mediated effects on the activity of insulin-like signaling in the intestine.
###end p 9

###xml 1933 1946 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1981 1995 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 2000 2011 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 2063 2074 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 2149 2163 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 2279 2293 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 2437 2450 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 2509 2523 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 2527 2538 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
An important component of the innate immune response in plants and animals is the induced expression of host defense effectors following pathogenic challenge [38]. Several genes that are induced following infection and are important to protect C. elegans from pathogenic challenge have been identified. These host defense effectors include defensin (abf-2), saposin (spp-1), and several genes with homology to antimicrobial proteins: lysozymes (lys-2 and lys-7), thaumatin (thn-2), and a CUB-domain containing protein, F08G5.6. The expression of abf-2 and spp-1 was induced following infection by the Gram-negative bacterium Salmonella typhimurium, and both genes were required to protect against S. typhimurium infection [20]. Independent microarray studies showed that lys-2 and F08G5.6 were induced following infection by P. aeruginosa and that thn-2 and lys-7 were induced by the Gram-positive pathogens E. faecalis and M. nematophilum[7]-[9],[21]. Interestingly, spp-1, thn-2, and lys-7 expression was repressed during infection by P. aeruginosa[7],[8],[39]. This expression pattern is unexpected given that these genes are required for optimal survival on P. aeruginosa (Figure S1). To confirm the expression data, we used quantitative RT-PCR (qRT-PCR) to measure the expression of these genes in worms exposed to P. aeruginosa (PA14), E. faecalis (V583), and S. typhimurium (SL1344) for 12 hours at 25degreesC (Figure 1A-B). Three of the genes (thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1) were significantly repressed by exposure to P. aeruginosa compared to the laboratory food source E. coli (OP50-1) (Figure 1A). Three of the genes (abf-2, F08G5.6, and lys-2) were significantly induced by exposure to P. aeruginosa (Figure 1B). In contrast to P. aeruginosa, none of the six genes tested were significantly repressed following exposure to either S. typhimurium or E. faecalis. Among the genes that were significantly repressed by exposure to P. aeruginosa, lys-7 was induced by exposure to S. typhimurium and E. faecalis, while thn-2 and spp-1 were induced by exposure to E. faecalis (Figure 1A). Though we did not detect a significant induction of spp-1 by S. typhimurium following 12-hour exposure (Figure 1A), spp-1 has been previously observed to be induced after 48-hour exposure to S. typhimurium[20]. Thus, the downregulation of known immune effectors appears to be an atypical response to infection that is characteristic of infection by P. aeruginosa because similar responses are not observed by exposure to S. typhimurium or E. faecalis.
###end p 12

###xml 1507 1511 1507 1511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1513 1517 1513 1517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1523 1527 1523 1527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 1570 1575 1570 1575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1585 1589 1585 1589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1594 1598 1594 1598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1621 1625 1621 1625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 0 13 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 96 106 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 475 485 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 575 588 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 651 664 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 691 695 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 783 787 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 849 853 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 994 998 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1012 1022 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1064 1068 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1403 1407 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
P. aeruginosa GacA is a two-component response regulator that is required for full virulence in C. elegans and mammals [40]-[42]. GacA regulates the production of molecules that are detrimental to the host, including pyocyanin, elastase, and exotoxin A [27],[28]. We wondered whether the suppression of host defense effectors is an active outcome of infection: specifically, whether GacA regulates factors that are important in downregulating host defense gene expression in C. elegans. We therefore compared the expression of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 in worms exposed to the P. aeruginosa gacA mutant for 12 hours (Figure 1C). In contrast to wildtype P. aeruginosa (hereafter referred to as PA14), none of the genes were repressed by exposure to an in-frame deletion mutant of gacA (PA14 gacA). This indicates that downregulation of immune genes by PA14 requires gacA. The quorum-sensing regulators encoded by lasR and rhlR function downstream of GacA [27]. lasR and rhlR are also required for PA14 virulence in C. elegans ([42] and Table S1). As with exposure to PA14 gacA, thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 were not repressed in worms exposed to a lasR transposon insertion mutant (PA14lasR) compared to OP50-1 (Figure 1C). In worms exposed to a rhlR transposon-insertion mutant (PA14rhlR), neither thn-2 nor lys-7 was downregulated, but spp-1 remained significantly repressed (Figure 1C). Thus, the ability of PA14 infection to downregulate the expression of thn-2 and lys-7 requires factors that are dependent on gacA, lasR, and rhlR. By contrast, while the downregulation of spp-1 requires gacA and lasR, it is independent of rhlR.
###end p 16

###xml 1154 1158 1154 1158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1165 1169 1165 1169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1180 1184 1180 1184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 1314 1328 1314 1328 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 1333 1344 1333 1344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. faecalis</italic>
###xml 1376 1381 1376 1381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1383 1388 1383 1388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1394 1399 1394 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1412 1421 1412 1421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 1655 1669 1655 1669 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 1673 1684 1673 1684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. faecalis</italic>
###xml 1743 1753 1743 1753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 4 8 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 18 22 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 127 131 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 138 142 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 153 157 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 324 334 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 391 395 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 397 401 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 408 412 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 423 427 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 930 934 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 941 945 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 955 959 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1149 1153 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1160 1164 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1175 1179 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1314 1328 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 1333 1344 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 1620 1624 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1655 1669 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 1673 1684 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 1743 1753 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The PA14 gacA and PA14 lasR mutant strains are unable to colonize the worm intestine [42]. To determine whether the failure of PA14 gacA, PA14 lasR, and PA14 rhlR mutants to downregulate immune gene expression is a consequence of a low inoculum in the intestine, we compared the expression of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 in the C. elegans tnt-3(aj3) mutant following infection with the wildtype PA14, PA14 gacA, PA14 lasR, and PA14 rhlR strains. The tnt-3(aj3) mutant is unable to grind bacteria, thus a large inoculum of live bacteria, including the nonpathogenic OP50-1, accumulate in the intestinal lumen [13],[20]. First, we observed that although the tnt-3(aj3) animals accumulate OP50-1 in the intestine, expression of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 was indistinguishable from expression in wildtype worms which do not accumulate OP50-1 (t-test, p = 0.46, 0.43, and 0.07, respectively). Importantly, despite the accumulation of intact PA14 gacA, PA14 lasR, or PA14 rhlR mutant bacteria within the intestinal lumen of tnt-3(aj3) animals, the expression of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 was not repressed (Figure S2). Thus, the lack of immune suppression by the PA14 gacA, PA14 lasR, and PA14 rhlR mutants is not due simply to limited intestinal colonization of wildtype worms. These results, coupled with the observation that S. typhimurium and E. faecalis infections do not downregulate thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 expression (Figure 1A), indicate that the mere presence of live bacteria in the intestinal lumen is insufficient to suppress the expression of a subset of immune genes. We conclude that a genetically regulated aspect of PA14 virulence, which is absent in S. typhimurium or E. faecalis, causes downregulation of a subset of immune effectors in C. elegans.
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 264 268 260 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Grant1">[43]</xref>
###xml 269 273 265 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Angot1">[44]</xref>
###xml 279 292 275 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 376 380 372 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Fauvarque1">[45]</xref>
###xml 381 385 377 381 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lee1">[48]</xref>
###xml 505 509 501 505 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Bleves1">[49]</xref>
###xml 510 514 506 510 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Yahr1">[50]</xref>
###xml 578 591 574 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 771 781 767 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 826 836 822 832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 845 849 841 845 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Miyata1">[46]</xref>
###xml 850 854 846 850 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wareham1">[51]</xref>
###xml 942 952 938 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1157 1167 1153 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1336 1345 1332 1337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;pscD</italic>
###xml 1412 1422 1404 1414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1424 1428 1416 1420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Miyata1">[46]</xref>
###xml 1468 1477 1460 1465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;pscD</italic>
###xml 1544 1549 1532 1537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1554 1559 1542 1547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1585 1595 1573 1583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 1628 1641 1616 1629 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1710 1741 1698 1717 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;exoT, &#916;exoU, &#916;exoY</italic>
###xml 1747 1756 1723 1728 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;pscD</italic>
###xml 1807 1812 1779 1784 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1827 1837 1799 1809 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 279 292 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 578 591 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 624 628 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 771 781 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 826 836 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 942 952 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1157 1167 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1412 1422 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1628 1641 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Several Gram-negative bacterial pathogens suppress host immunity by employing the type III secretion system (T3SS), which injects virulence effectors directly into host cytoplasm to inhibit or limit the duration of NF-kappaB and MAP kinase activation (reviewed in [43],[44]). In P. aeruginosa, T3SS is an important virulence determinant in pathogenesis in insects and mammals [45]-[48]. Type III secretion genes are under the control of the GacS/GacA two-component regulator and the quorum-sensing system [49],[50]. To date, four T3SS effector proteins have been identified for P. aeruginosa: ExoS, ExoT, ExoU, and ExoY. In PA14, only ExoT, ExoU, and ExoY are encoded in the genome and their expression requires PscD. Although the T3SS is induced during infection of the C. elegans intestine, it appears to be dispensable for C. elegans killing [46],[51]. This led to the proposal that other virulence factors that play a predominant role in C. elegans pathogenesis could mask the effect of type III secretion effectors when death was used as the metric for the pathogenesis assay. We therefore determined whether the T3SS contributes to the suppression of C. elegans immune effectors, an arguably more sensitive assay. As previously observed, neither loss of any of the Type III effectors nor the entire repertoire of effectors in the DeltapscD mutant significantly affects the ability of these strains to kill C. elegans ([46] and data not shown). We found that the DeltapscD mutant was still able to significantly suppress the expression of lys-7 and spp-1, as measured by qRT-PCR (Figure S3A). We further confirmed that the P. aeruginosa T3SS is not required for immune suppression by showing that neither DeltaexoT, DeltaexoU, DeltaexoY, nor DeltapscD mutant significantly affected the expression of a lys-7 GFP-reporter (Figure S3B).
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 3 13 3 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 89 102 85 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 254 258 250 254 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Apidianakis1">[36]</xref>
###xml 349 354 345 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 358 363 354 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 400 410 396 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3A</xref>
###xml 451 456 447 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 458 468 454 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 529 539 525 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 3 13 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 89 102 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 529 539 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
In Drosophila, downregulation of NF-kappaB-regulated antimicrobial peptide expression by P. aeruginosa is mediated by an unknown mechanism that requires an S-adenosyl-methionine-dependent methyltransferase domain-containing protein encoded by PA14_41070 [36]. A PA14_41070 transposon insertion mutant is not defective in the ability to downregulate lys-7 or spp-1 expression, as measured by qRT-PCR (Figure S3A) and by GFP-reporter gene expression of lys-7 (Figure S3B). Thus, PA14_41070 is dispensable for immune suppression in C. elegans.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 93 106 93 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 165 175 165 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 257 261 257 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA</italic>
###xml 266 270 266 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqsA</italic>
###xml 286 290 286 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA</italic>
###xml 368 372 368 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kay1">[52]</xref>
###xml 577 588 577 588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
###xml 740 744 740 744 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-McGrath1">[53]</xref>
###xml 745 749 745 749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wade1">[54]</xref>
###xml 799 812 799 812 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 889 897 889 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqsABCDE</italic>
###xml 905 909 905 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-DArgenio1">[55]</xref>
###xml 910 914 910 914 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Coleman1">[57]</xref>
###xml 925 929 925 929 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA</italic>
###xml 934 938 934 938 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqsA</italic>
###xml 981 991 981 991 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 993 997 993 997 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Tan2">[42]</xref>
###xml 1002 1010 1002 1010 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s012">Table S1</xref>
###xml 1030 1034 1030 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA</italic>
###xml 1043 1047 1043 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqsA</italic>
###xml 1100 1105 1100 1105 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1149 1159 1149 1159 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 1275 1285 1275 1285 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1301 1305 1301 1305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA</italic>
###xml 1310 1314 1310 1314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqsA</italic>
###xml 93 106 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 165 175 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 799 812 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 981 991 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1275 1285 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
To determine whether suppression of host defense gene expression is strictly associated with P. aeruginosa virulence, we tested several mutants that are impaired in C. elegans killing. First, we tested two genes that are part of the GacA-LasR-RhlR regulon: dsbA and pqsA. Expression of dsbA, which encodes a periplasmic dithiol:disulfide oxidoreductase, requires GacA [52]. DsbA is required for the formation of disulfide bonds in periplasmic proteins and important for proper folding of multiple virulence factors exported by Type II secretion, including elastase and lipase. Pseudomonas quinolone signal (PQS) system is the third component of the quorum-sensing signaling system, and it is regulated by Las and Rhl quorum-sensing systems [53],[54]. Production of all known quinolone/quinolines in P. aeruginosa requires PqsA, an anthranilate-coenzyme A ligase that is the product of the pqsABCDE operon [55]-[57]. Both the dsbA and pqsA mutant strains are attenuated for killing C. elegans ([42] and Table S1). Yet, neither the dsbA nor the pqsA mutants is defective in the ability to downregulate lys-7 expression, as measured by a GFP-reporter (Figure S3B). Thus, PQS and DsbA, despite their requirement for virulence are not necessary for host immune suppression in the C. elegans model. Because dsbA and pqsA are part of the GacA-LasR-RhlR regulon, these results suggest that only a subset of the genes regulated by the GacA two-component and acyl-homoserine lactone quorum-sensing systems are required for immune suppression.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 201 205 201 205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Schuster1">[58]</xref>
###xml 206 210 206 210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wagner1">[59]</xref>
###xml 273 283 273 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 285 293 285 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s012">Table S1</xref>
###xml 357 362 357 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 405 415 405 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 467 480 467 480 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 652 665 652 665 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 273 283 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 467 480 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 652 665 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
To determine the specificity of the GacA-LasR-RhlR regulon in immune suppression, we tested three additional genes that are not known to be part of this regulon: PA14_23420, PA14_23430, and PA14_59010 [58],[59]. We found that while these mutants are attenuated for killing C. elegans (Table S1), they had no detectable defect in the ability to downregulate lys-7 expression as measured by a GFP-reporter (Figure S3B). Overall these results indicate that virulence in P. aeruginosa is not strictly associated with immune suppression and that a subset of the GacA-, LasR- and RhlR-dependent factors are required for the downregulation of immune genes by P. aeruginosa.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
###xml 0 13 0 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 0 13 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
P. aeruginosa downregulates a subset of DAF-2-dependent immune genes
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 3 13 3 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 177 181 174 178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Ewbank1">[11]</xref>
###xml 182 186 179 183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-GravatoNobre1">[12]</xref>
###xml 268 273 265 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 393 396 390 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 468 473 465 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 482 486 479 483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Murphy1">[16]</xref>
###xml 487 491 484 488 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-McElwee1">[60]</xref>
###xml 526 529 523 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 530 533 527 530 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 549 554 546 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 711 719 708 716 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s017">Table S6</xref>
###xml 721 729 718 726 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s018">Table S7</xref>
###xml 731 742 728 739 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s011">Figure S10A</xref>
###xml 923 928 920 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 990 995 987 992 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 1145 1153 1142 1150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s019">Table S8</xref>
###xml 1155 1166 1152 1163 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s011">Figure S10B</xref>
###xml 1185 1192 1182 1189 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s001">Text S1</xref>
###xml 3 13 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 250 254 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 495 499 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 567 571 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 795 799 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1000 1004 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1090 1094 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
In C. elegans, at least three conserved signaling pathways contribute to host defense: p38 MAPK signaling, Sma/TGF-beta signaling, and DAF-2 insulin-like signaling (reviewed in [11],[12]). We had previously noted that the transcriptional profiles of PA14-infected and daf-2 loss-of-function worms were overlapping, but the genes regulated in common tend to be regulated in opposite directions [7]. Here, we compared whole-genome transcriptional profiles of uninfected daf-2 mutants [16],[60] to PA14-infected wildtype animals [7],[8] and found that daf-2 mutants and PA14 infection have predominately discordant effects on gene expression across a range of data sets using a variety of criteria for comparison (Table S6, Table S7, Figure S10A). This suggests that the gene expression pattern in PA14-infected animals is opposite of the pattern produced by reducing the activity of DAF-2, such as occurs in loss-of-function daf-2 mutants. Importantly, genes that were inversely regulated by daf-2 and PA14 infection were enriched for immune effector genes, thus raising the possibility that PA14 infection activates DAF-2 insulin-like signaling (Table S8, Figure S10B; for details, see Text S1).
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 222 234 222 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 315 320 315 320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 442 454 442 454 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 562 574 562 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1134 1146 1134 1146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1174 1183 1174 1183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 1312 1324 1312 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1335 1336 1335 1336 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 1485 1497 1485 1497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1533 1534 1533 1534 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 1772 1777 1772 1777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 62 66 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 126 130 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 261 265 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 342 346 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 415 419 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 526 530 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 782 786 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1034 1038 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1126 1130 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1285 1289 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1389 1393 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1720 1724 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1808 1812 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1848 1852 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1913 1917 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2083 2087 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
If indeed activation of DAF-2 insulin-like signaling mediates PA14 suppression of host defense effectors, then the ability of PA14 to suppress host defense effectors would be attenuated or eliminated when loss-of-function daf-2(e1370) mutants are infected with PA14. Alternatively, if the transcriptional effect of daf-2 loss of function and PA14 infection operate in parallel, then the transcriptional response to PA14 will be unaffected in daf-2(e1370) animals. We therefore compared the change in gene expression following PA14 infection between wildtype and daf-2(e1370) animals using whole-genome microarrays. First, using the criteria of t-test p-values<0.05 and 2-fold up- or down-regulation, we identified 247 induced and 137 repressed genes in wildtype worms infected with PA14 for 24 hours compared to uninfected controls. We confirmed that the selection of these criteria did not affect our conclusions by repeating the analysis with a range of p-value and fold-change thresholds (data not shown). Next, using this list of PA14-induced and -repressed genes, we compared the change in gene expression in response to PA14 in daf-2(e1370) and wildtype (N2) animals (Figure 2A). Separate linear regressions of induced and repressed genes revealed that the induction response to PA14 was largely intact in daf-2(e1370) animals (r2 = 0.4280, p<0.0001), but the repression response to PA14 was substantially attenuated to the extent that the repression response observed in N2 and daf-2(e1370) was not significantly associated (r2 = 0.001, p = 0.3). Comparison of induced and repressed genes provides an internal control for this analysis and indicates that attenuation of the downregulation of genes in response to PA14 infection does not simply reflect a failure of daf-2 animals to become infected by PA14 or to respond transcriptionally to PA14 infection. These results are consistent with the model that PA14 infection suppresses host defense genes through activation of the DAF-2 insulin-like signaling pathway. It also indicates that the induction of genes in response to PA14 infection is largely independent of DAF-2.
###end p 24
###begin title 25
###xml 71 76 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
The downregulation of host defense genes is specifically attenuated in daf-2 insulin-like signaling mutants.
###end title 25

###xml 1324 1325 1324 1325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 1355 1365 1355 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 1482 1492 1482 1492 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 38 42 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 503 507 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>

(A-B) The transcriptional response to PA14 infection in wildtype N2 versus (A) daf-2(e1370) and (B) sma-6(wk7) worms is plotted based on whole-genome microarray analysis. Values are log2 scale transformations of the response to infection. The subset of genes that were differentially regulated in N2 worms is shown (p<0.05 and absolute difference >2 fold). Linear regressions are plotted for induced (red) and repressed (green) genes independently. (A) In daf-2(e1370), the response to induced genes to PA14 infection was largely intact (r2 = 0.4280, p<0.0001), but the response to repressed genes was strongly attenuated (r2 = 0.0009, p = 0.8306). (B) In sma-6(wk7), the response of both induced and repressed genes was largely intact (p<0.0001). (C-E) The transcriptional response to PA14 infection in wildtype N2 and (A) daf-2(e1370), (B) sek-1(km4), and (C) sma-6(wk7) animals is plotted for a set of 146 candidate immune and stress response genes based on qRT-PCR measurement. Linear regressions were calculated for induced (red) and repressed (green) genes independently. The associated correlation coefficients (r2) and p-values are indicated. (C) In daf-2(e1370), the response to induced genes to PA14 infection was largely intact (r2 = 0.62, p<0.0001), but the response to repressed genes was strongly attenuated (r2 = 0.061, p = 0.1103). (D) In sek-1(km4) the response of both induced and repressed genes was largely intact (p<0.0001 and p = 0.0026, respectively). (E) In sma-6(wk7) the response of both induced and repressed genes was largely intact (p<0.0001 each).
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 243 253 237 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 307 319 301 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 439 449 433 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 452 453 446 447 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 504 513 498 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2B</xref>
###xml 653 665 647 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 671 681 665 675 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 743 755 737 749 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 760 770 754 764 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 782 783 776 777 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 798 799 792 793 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 940 952 934 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 987 997 981 991 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 1005 1007 999 1001 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 127 131 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 401 405 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1169 1173 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
To examine whether the Sma/TGF-beta signaling pathway could also contribute to the suppression of host defense genes following PA14 infection, we compared whole-genome expression data from infected and uninfected TGF-beta receptor null mutant sma-6(wk7) and wildtype worms. Using the same parameters as the daf-2(e1370) analysis, we note that both the induction and repression of genes in response to PA14 infection were largely intact in sma-6(wk7) (r2 = 0.5231 and 0.4051, respectively, p<0.0001 each; Figure 2B). The correlation coefficients for induced and repressed genes were not significantly different. Comparison of the regression results from daf-2(e1370) with sma-6(wk7) is revealing. The correlations for induced genes between the daf-2(e1370) and sma-6(wk7) analyses (r2 = 0.4280 and r2 = 0.5231, respectively) were not significantly different (p = 0.09, one-tailed test). Among the repressed genes, however, correlations with daf-2(e1370) were significantly less than with sma-6(wk7) (p = 10-5, one-tailed test). Together, the data indicate that the Sma/TGF-beta pathway is unlikely to contribute substantially to the suppression of host defense genes by PA14 infection.
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 494 497 494 497 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
