###xml 2397 2409 2397 2409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 2411 2420 2411 2420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2C</xref>
###xml 2455 2466 2455 2466 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pmk-1(km25)</italic>
###xml 2503 2513 2503 2513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 2549 2559 2549 2559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pmk-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 2587 2588 2587 2588 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 2628 2638 2628 2638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 928 932 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1231 1235 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1423 1427 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1537 1541 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1913 1917 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2531 2535 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
To corroborate the results obtained from whole-genome microarray analysis, and also to analyze the involvement of p38 MAPK signaling, we repeated the transcriptional profile analysis using qRT-PCR measurement of a panel of 146 infection and stress response genes. We designed gene-specific qRT-PCR primers to a panel of 146 genes selected on the basis of their likely involvement in the response to infection and stress. Many immune and stress response genes are members of large gene families [7],[61]. The use of gene-specific qRT-PCR primers overcomes the problem of cross hybridization of gene families in microarray studies and provides more precise measures of mRNA levels. Moreover, the use of genes with known or putative function in immune and stress response supports the inference that observed transcriptional effects are functionally important. We measured gene expression in young adult worms exposed to OP50-1 or PA14 for 12 hours for N2, daf-2(e1370), sma-6(wk7), and sek-1(km4), a p38 MAPKK null mutant, to obtain the change in gene expression following infection for each worm strain (Table S2). We repeated the linear regression analysis of induced and repressed genes, comparing the transcriptional response to PA14 in each mutant to N2 (Figure 2C-2E). Transcriptional analysis of daf-2(e1370) using this targeted gene set indicated that the induction of immune and stress response genes in response to PA14 was largely intact in daf-2(e1370) animals (r2 = 0.62, p<0.0001), but the repression of genes in response to PA14 was substantially attenuated to the extent that the correlation between N2 and daf-2(e1370) was not statistically significant (r2 = 0.061, p = 0.11; Figure 2C). This pattern of gene expression mirrors the result of the whole-genome analysis (Figure 2A) and provides further support that a substantial subset of the normal downregulation of gene expression in response to PA14 infection requires daf-2, but the upregulation of gene expression is largely independent of daf-2. In contrast to daf-2(e1370), both induced and repressed genes in sek-1(km4) and sma-6(wk7) mutants correlated significantly with N2 (Figure 2D-2E), thus corroborating the results of our whole-genome analysis with sma-6(wk7). Visually, the induced and repressed linear regression lines are concordant for sek-1(km4) (Figure 2D) and sma-6(wk7) (Figure 2E), but highly discordant in daf-2(e1370) (Figure 2C). Analysis with a p38 MAPK mutant pmk-1(km25) yielded nearly identical results to sek-1(km4): the response to PA14 infection in pmk-1(km4) correlated significantly (r2 = 0.80, p<0.0001) with the response in sek-1(km4) (data not shown).
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 33 45 33 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6, sek-1</italic>
###xml 50 55 50 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 271 277 271 277 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mutant</sub>
###xml 294 302 294 302 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wildtype</sub>
###xml 337 358 337 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="sec" rid="s4">Materials and Methods</xref>
###xml 413 418 413 414 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 422 428 418 424 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mutant</sub>
###xml 430 438 426 434 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wildtype</sub>
###xml 616 621 612 613 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 679 684 671 672 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 98 102 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 237 241 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
To detect more subtle effects of sma-6, sek-1 and daf-2 mutations on transcriptional responses to PA14 we compared the average differential expression of the immune and stress response genes under normal (OP50-1 exposure) and infection (PA14) conditions between mutant (Xmutant) and wildtype (Xwildtype) worms using a paired t-test (see Materials and Methods). The average difference in induction or repression (XDelta = Xmutant-Xwildtype) was calculated for each mutant-wildtype pair. This approach accounts for both the magnitude and direction of attenuation of the response to infection, with positive values of XDelta indicating attenuated repression and negative values of XDelta indicating attenuated induction.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 3 13 3 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 204 209 204 205 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 250 260 246 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 328 333 324 325 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 365 370 357 358 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 447 456 435 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk)</italic>
###xml 460 464 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
In sma-6(wk7) mutants, the correlation analysis indicated that both induction and repression were largely intact. Consistent with this analysis, the average difference in either induction or repression (XDelta) of immune and stress response genes in sma-6(wk7) mutants was not significantly different from wildtype (induction: XDelta = 0.09, p = 0.38; repression: XDelta = 0.00, p = 0.99). It remains possible that the increased susceptibility of sma-6(wk) to PA14 may be a consequence of deregulation of immune gene expression that could not be detected by this analysis.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 3 13 3 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 127 132 127 128 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 146 148 142 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;4</sup>
###xml 310 320 306 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 401 406 397 398 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 818 821 810 813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 869 874 861 866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1</italic>
###xml 905 912 897 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">clec-85</italic>
###xml 914 919 906 911 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-1</italic>
###xml 921 926 913 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-8</italic>
###xml 952 958 944 950 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-38</italic>
###xml 997 1003 989 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-38</italic>
###xml 1096 1101 1088 1093 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1</italic>
###xml 1103 1117 1095 1109 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s005">Figure S4A&#8211;S4F</xref>
###xml 1233 1238 1225 1230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1</italic>
###xml 1308 1313 1300 1305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1</italic>
###xml 1328 1333 1320 1325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 1335 1340 1327 1332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cpr-3</italic>
###xml 1342 1348 1334 1340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-18</italic>
###xml 1373 1387 1365 1379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s005">Figure S4G&#8211;S4K</xref>
###xml 1424 1429 1416 1421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 1433 1443 1425 1435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 1566 1571 1558 1563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 1618 1623 1610 1615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sek-1</italic>
###xml 1638 1648 1630 1640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s005">Figure S4G</xref>
###xml 529 533 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 688 692 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 813 817 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 892 896 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1288 1292 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1542 1546 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
In sek-1(km4) mutants, the average induction in response to infection is significantly less than that of wildtype (induction: XDelta = -0.61, p<10-4), indicating that the induction response is attenuated when p38 signaling is abrogated. Although there is a trend towards attenuation of host gene repression in sek-1(km4), the overall effect is not statistically significant for this set of 42 genes (XDelta = 0.38, p = 0.16). Thus, a definitive conclusion regarding the requirement of p38 in repression of immune genes following PA14 infection awaits a whole-genome analysis. By this analysis we are able to show that p38 MAPK signaling is required for the induction of many genes during PA14 infection, consistent with a previous report that p38 MAPK is an important regulator of the transcriptional response to PA14 [8]. Immune and stress response genes that require sek-1 for induction by PA14 include clec-85, lys-1, lys-8, F35E12.5, Y40D12A.2 and gst-38. Interestingly, with the exception of gst-38, the basal expression of these genes under normal growth conditions on OP50-1 also requires sek-1 (Figure S4A-S4F). We also identified a class of genes whose expression levels during normal growth and following infection require sek-1 but whose induction or repression in response to PA14 do not require sek-1; they include lys-2, cpr-3, spp-18, F55G11.2, and T10D3.6 (Figure S4G-S4K). For example, expression levels of lys-2 in sek-1(km4) animals are 0.5% of levels in wildtype worms both in worms exposed to OP50-1 and worms exposed to PA14, yet expression of lys-2 is induced by a similar ratio in wildtype and sek-1 mutant worms (Figure S4G).
###end p 31
###begin p 32
###xml 91 103 91 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 173 178 173 174 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 213 218 209 210 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 231 233 223 225 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;5</sup>
###xml 358 370 350 362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 396 401 388 393 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 504 509 496 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abf-2</italic>
###xml 511 516 503 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 549 557 541 549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s013">Table S2</xref>
###xml 574 586 566 578 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 771 776 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 800 805 792 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 807 818 799 810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7 spp-1</italic>
###xml 824 829 816 821 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 831 839 823 831 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s013">Table S2</xref>
###xml 861 883 853 875 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7), sek-1(km4)</italic>
###xml 889 901 881 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 908 920 900 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1163 1167 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
The average differences in induction and repression of immune and stress response genes in daf-2(e1370) mutants were both significantly different from wildtype (induction: XDelta = -0.36, p = 0.0004; repression: XDelta = 1.32, p<10-5). Thus, by this analysis we are able to detect a small but significant attenuation in gene induction following infection in daf-2(e1370) mutants, suggesting that daf-2 activity is required for the induction of a small subset of infection-responsive genes, which include abf-2, lys-2, F08G5.6, ZK6.11, and C17H12.8 (Table S2). The effect of daf-2(e1370) on repression of gene expression in response to infection was the strongest observed effect, consistent with the regression analysis. The immune and stress response genes that require daf-2 for repression include thn-2, lys-7 spp-1, and gst-4 (Table S2). Importantly, among sma-6(wk7), sek-1(km4), and daf-2(e1370), only daf-2(e1370) significantly attenuated repression of infection response genes. Together, the transcriptional analyses confirm that of the three immune signaling pathways, DAF-2 insulin-like signaling is required for the downregulation of many genes during PA14 infection.
###end p 32
###begin title 33
Suppression of some host defense genes is DAF-16-dependent
###end title 33
###begin p 34
###xml 17 22 17 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 142 146 142 146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Garsin1">[15]</xref>
###xml 274 279 274 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">age-1</italic>
###xml 279 283 279 283 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Morris1">[62]</xref>
###xml 284 288 284 288 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wolkow1">[63]</xref>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Paradis1">[64]</xref>
###xml 419 423 419 423 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Hertweck1">[66]</xref>
###xml 539 543 539 543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lee2">[67]</xref>
###xml 544 548 544 548 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lin1">[68]</xref>
###xml 666 671 666 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 673 678 673 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 684 689 684 689 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 708 720 708 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 722 734 722 734 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 754 766 754 766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 767 779 767 779 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 881 886 881 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 888 893 888 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 899 904 899 904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 939 951 939 951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 953 965 953 965 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3A&#8211;3C</xref>
###xml 984 989 984 989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 1138 1150 1138 1150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1258 1270 1258 1270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1319 1324 1319 1324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1326 1332 1326 1332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7,</italic>
###xml 1337 1342 1337 1342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1409 1418 1409 1418 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s006">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 1524 1536 1524 1536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1583 1588 1583 1588 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1593 1598 1593 1598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1633 1645 1633 1645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 1678 1684 1678 1684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 1745 1757 1745 1757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3A&#8211;3B</xref>
###xml 1805 1810 1805 1810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1815 1820 1815 1820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1854 1866 1854 1866 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 1899 1904 1899 1904 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1909 1914 1909 1914 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1932 1938 1932 1938 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 1940 1952 1940 1952 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3A&#8211;3B</xref>
###xml 1984 1989 1984 1989 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1993 2005 1993 2005 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 2006 2018 2006 2018 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 2107 2112 2107 2112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 2239 2244 2239 2244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 2273 2278 2273 2278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 2365 2370 2365 2370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2429 2441 2429 2441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 2483 2488 2483 2488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2507 2513 2507 2513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 2515 2524 2515 2524 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3C</xref>
###xml 2559 2563 2559 2563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Alper1">[39]</xref>
###xml 2600 2605 2600 2605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2652 2664 2652 2664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 2669 2694 2669 2694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 2748 2753 2748 2753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2757 2762 2757 2762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 2794 2800 2794 2800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 2877 2882 2877 2882 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 2884 2889 2884 2889 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 2895 2900 2895 2900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2976 2981 2976 2981 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 2986 2991 2986 2991 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 3037 3042 3037 3042 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 857 861 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 908 912 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1196 1200 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1228 1232 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1540 1544 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1785 1789 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1918 1922 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2145 2149 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2908 2912 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Loss-of-function daf-2 mutants are resistant to bacterial pathogens, and this resistance is dependent on the FOXO transcription factor DAF-16 [15]. DAF-2 regulates DAF-16 at least in part through the activation of phosphoinositide 3-kinase (PI3-kinase), which is encoded by age-1[62],[63]. PI3-kinase potentiates the activity of several serine threonine kinases, including homologs of mammalian PDK1, AKT, and SGK [64]-[66]. These kinases phosphorylate DAF-16, retaining it in the cytoplasm and suppressing DAF-16 transcriptional activity [67],[68]. To determine whether DAF-16 is required for the suppression of host defense genes, we quantified the mRNA levels of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 by qRT-PCR in N2, daf-2(e1370), daf-16(mu86), and double mutant daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370) worms under normal growth conditions (on OP50-1) or following infection with PA14. Downregulation of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 by PA14 exposure was abolished in daf-2(e1370) (Figure 3A-3C), confirming that daf-2 activity is required for the downregulation of a number of functionally important immune genes. Next, we inactivated each of these genes by RNAi in daf-2(e1370) and compared the degree of colonization by a PA14 strain that expresses GFP (PA14-GFP) in these animals to daf-2(e1370) animals exposed to vector control. Knockdown of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 individually resulted in a significant increased in colonization (Figure S5), indicating that the ability to prevent downregulation of immune genes contributes to the resistance of daf-2(e1370) to PA14. Under normal growth conditions, both thn-2 and lys-7 were expressed at lower levels in daf-16(mu86) compared to N2, indicating that daf-16 is required for basal expression of these immune effectors (Figure 3A-3B). Following infection with PA14, the levels of thn-2 and lys-7 mRNA were not reduced further in daf-16(mu86), indicating that suppression of thn-2 and lys-7 by PA14 requires daf-16 (Figure 3A-3B). Curiously, the expression of lys-7 in daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370) double mutants was intermediate to the expression in either single mutant. Nonetheless, lys-7 expression was not repressed by PA14 infection in either single or double mutants. These results suggest that basal levels of lys-7 expression are regulated by daf-2-dependent factors in addition to DAF-16. By contrast, under normal growth conditions, spp-1 expression was not significantly different between N2 and daf-16(mu86), indicating that the basal expression of spp-1 is independent of daf-16 (Figure 3C), in contrast to previous reports [39]. Curiously, as in wildtype animals, spp-1 expression was significantly downregulated in daf-16(mu86) and daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370) mutants, indicating that while the downregulation of spp-1 is daf-2-dependent, it does not require daf-16. Overall, these results implicate DAF-2 and DAF-16 in the downregulation of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 during PA14 infection. DAF-16 appears to be required for the expression of thn-2 and lys-7, but the role of DAF-16 in the regulation of spp-1 expression is more complex.
###end p 34

###xml 106 111 106 111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>

###xml 147 159 147 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 165 177 165 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>

###begin p 37
###xml 45 50 45 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abf-2</italic>
###xml 65 70 65 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 104 109 104 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 114 120 114 120 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 122 134 122 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3D&#8211;3F</xref>
###xml 180 185 180 185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abf-2</italic>
###xml 219 231 219 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>

###xml 251 276 251 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 339 344 339 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abf-2</italic>
###xml 397 406 397 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3D</xref>
###xml 476 488 476 488 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 533 538 533 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 547 553 547 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 555 564 555 564 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3E</xref>
###xml 596 601 596 601 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 606 612 606 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 673 678 673 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 730 735 730 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 847 852 847 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 938 943 938 943 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 958 970 958 970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1106 1111 1106 1111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-2</italic>
###xml 1115 1127 1115 1127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1129 1138 1129 1138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3F</xref>
###xml 74 78 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1060 1064 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1267 1271 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Next, we determined whether the induction of abf-2, F08G5.6, and lys-2 by PA14 infection is mediated by daf-2 and daf-16 (Figure 3D-3F). In contrast to wildtype, the expression of abf-2 was not significantly induced in daf-2(e1370), daf-16(mu86), and daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370) mutants following infection, suggesting that the induction of abf-2 is modulated by the DAF-2/DAF-16 signaling pathway (Figure 3D). The induction of F08G5.6 was not statistically significant only in daf-2(e1370), suggesting that F08G5.6 induction requires daf-2 but not daf-16 (Figure 3E). The expression of F08G5.6 in daf-2 and daf-16 single and double mutants mirrors the expression pattern of spp-1. Thus, the induction of some genes is dependent on daf-2 as suggested by the paired t-test analysis performed on the immune and stress response gene set. Expression of lys-2 was largely unaffected in the insulin-like signaling mutants. However, expression of lys-2 was higher in daf-2(e1370) under basal conditions (on OP50-1). This difference was not observed in worms exposed to PA14, resulting in net a reduced induction of lys-2 in daf-2(e1370) (Figure 3F). Overall, the gene expression analyses suggest that while DAF-2 and DAF-16 are largely dispensable for the induced response to PA14 infection, some genes do require DAF-2 for induction.
###end p 37

###xml 0 11 0 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>

###xml 540 543 540 543 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 675 688 675 688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 787 791 787 791 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lau1">[30]</xref>
###xml 815 820 815 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sod-3</italic>
###xml 832 837 832 837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 890 895 890 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 936 945 936 945 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s006">Figure S5</xref>
###xml 1054 1059 1054 1059 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 1061 1066 1061 1066 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mtl-1</italic>
###xml 1072 1077 1072 1077 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ctl-1</italic>
###xml 1101 1106 1101 1106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 1115 1119 1115 1119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Murphy1">[16]</xref>
###xml 1152 1157 1152 1157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 1201 1205 1201 1205 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Leiers1">[72]</xref>
###xml 1294 1304 1294 1304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s008">Figure S7A</xref>
###xml 1328 1338 1328 1338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s008">Figure S7B</xref>
###xml 1359 1364 1359 1364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 1382 1386 1382 1386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1388 1392 1388 1392 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1398 1402 1398 1402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 1404 1414 1404 1414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s008">Figure S7A</xref>
###xml 1438 1450 1438 1450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1459 1471 1459 1471 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 1473 1483 1473 1483 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s008">Figure S7B</xref>
###xml 1506 1511 1506 1511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 1529 1542 1529 1542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 271 281 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 478 482 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 582 586 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 675 688 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 930 934 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1235 1239 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1368 1372 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1529 1542 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
In addition to immune effectors, the insulin-like signaling pathway also regulates stress response genes [16],[69]. For example, sod-3 encodes a well-characterized DAF-16-regulated superoxide dismutase that is associated with oxidative stress resistance and longevity in C. elegans, presumably through its reactive oxygen species detoxification activity [16],[70],[71]. We showed by qRT-PCR that the expression of sod-3 was significantly repressed following 24-hour exposure to PA14 (Figure S6), consistent with previous microarray studies [8]. This further supports the model that PA14 activates DAF-2 and inhibits DAF-16. Suppression of an antioxidant may be beneficial to P. aeruginosa, which produces pyocyanin as a virulence determinant that causes oxidative damage to host tissues [30]. However, knockdown of sod-3 by RNAi in daf-2 animals did not significantly affect the ability of daf-2 mutants to resist colonization by PA14 (Figure S5), perhaps because of the expression of other genes that contributes to oxidative stress resistance, such as gst-4, mtl-1, and ctl-1, are also increased in daf-2 mutants [16]. We note that the expression of gst-4, which encodes a glutathione-S transferase [72] is also downregulated during PA14 infection, as determined by reporter gene expression (Figure S7A) and qRT-PCR analyses (Figure S7B). Downregulation of gst-4 by PA14 requires gacA, lasR, and rhlR (Figure S7A), and is suppressed by daf-2(e1370) but not daf-16(mu86) (Figure S7B). Thus, activation of daf-2 signaling during P. aeruginosa infection results in the simultaneous downregulation of stress response and immune effectors genes that together could aid in the pathogenesis of these bacteria.
###end p 39
###begin title 40
###xml 0 13 0 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 0 13 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
P. aeruginosa infection causes delocalization of nuclear DAF-16
###end title 40
###begin p 41
###xml 31 36 31 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 77 81 77 81 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Murphy1">[16]</xref>
###xml 341 346 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 409 413 409 413 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lin1">[68]</xref>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Henderson1">[73]</xref>
###xml 508 512 508 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Henderson1">[73]</xref>
###xml 656 660 656 660 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Henderson1">[73]</xref>
###xml 750 753 750 753 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 754 757 754 757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 1297 1301 1297 1301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Hsin1">[74]</xref>
###xml 1302 1306 1302 1306 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Hsu1">[75]</xref>
###xml 1648 1652 1642 1646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1727 1736 1715 1724 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4A</xref>
###xml 1746 1750 1734 1738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1752 1761 1740 1749 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4B</xref>
###xml 1918 1930 1906 1918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4C&#8211;4D</xref>
###xml 2063 2072 2051 2060 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4E</xref>
###xml 2352 2369 2340 2357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figures 4C and 4D</xref>
###xml 2740 2744 2728 2732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 2778 2787 2766 2775 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4F</xref>
###xml 2886 2890 2874 2878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 542 546 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 692 696 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 799 803 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1634 1638 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1643 1647 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1741 1745 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1827 1831 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2170 2174 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2614 2618 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2735 2739 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2881 2885 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
The transcriptional effects of daf-2 mutants are largely dependent on DAF-16 [16]. Under normal growth conditions, the DAF-2 pathway is active and DAF-16 protein is distributed predominately in the cytoplasm of every tissue. Conditions that reduce signaling in the DAF-2 pathway, including heat stress, ablation of the germline, and loss of daf-2 function, cause DAF-16 protein to be localized in the nucleus [68],[73]. DAF-16 translocates from the nucleus to the cytoplasm when DAF-2 signaling is increased [73]. We determined the effect of PA14 infection on DAF-16 localization using transgenic worms that express a functional DAF-16::GFP fusion protein [73]. We confirmed that exposure to PA14 does not cause increased DAF-16 nuclear localization [7],[8]. Our gene expression data suggested that PA14 infection activates DAF-2 signaling and could consequently result in delocalization of DAF-16 from the nucleus. To measure this effect, it was necessary to first localize DAF-16 to the nucleus and then compare the reversal of that localization between infected and uninfected animals. We used two independent means to drive DAF-16::GFP to the nucleus: brief heat shock and removal of the germline, both of which are reported to induce DAF-16 nuclear localization in a DAF-2-independent manner [74],[75]. Heat shock causes transient nuclear localization that reverses over time, whereas the degree of nuclear localization caused by loss of germline proliferation is relatively stable in young worms. For the heat-shock approach, worms exposed to 37degreesC dry heat for 70 to 90 minutes were shifted onto plates containing OP50-1, PA14, or PA14 gacA. After 16 hours at 25degreesC, almost all of the worms exposed to OP50-1 (Figure 4A) or PA14 gacA (Figure 4B) retained nuclear DAF-16::GFP. By contrast, in a majority of the PA14-infected population, DAF-16::GFP was delocalized from the nuclei of intestinal cells (Figure 4C-4D). We quantified this effect by counting the number of intestinal nuclei in which DAF-16::GFP fluorescence was apparent. As shown in Figure 4E, the number of nuclei with visible DAF-16::GFP nuclear localization was significantly reduced in PA14-infected worms compared to OP50-fed worms (p<0.001). Because the distribution of nuclei containing DAF-16::GFP per worm was distinctly bimodal (representative examples shown in Figures 4C and 4D), individual worms could be classified as having predominately nuclear-localized or predominately nuclear-delocalized (i.e., cytoplasmic) DAF-16::GFP in subsequent assays. Following 16 hours recovery from acute heat shock, approximately 80% of PA14-infected worms no longer retained the DAF-16::GFP fusion protein in the nucleus, whereas worms exposed to OP50-1 or PA14 gacA were not significantly affected (Figure 4F, p<0.0001). DAF-16::GFP remains nuclear localized in heat-shocked worms exposed to OP50-1 or PA14 gacA for 48 to 60 hours.
###end p 41

###xml 0 13 0 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 0 13 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
P. aeruginosa infection causes delocalization of nuclear DAF-16 in the intestine.
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 172 176 172 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 789 793 783 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 822 826 816 820 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 836 840 830 834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 167 171 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 195 199 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 282 286 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 382 386 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 778 782 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 784 788 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 807 811 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">V583</span>
###xml 817 821 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 831 835 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
(A-D) Representative fluorescence micrographs of DAF-16::GFP expressing adult worms with nuclear localized DAF-16::GFP fusion protein after exposure to (A) OP50-1 (B) PA14 gacA, and (C) wildtype PA14, and also (D) nuclear delocalized DAF-16::GFP in worms after exposure to wildtype PA14. (E) Mean number of nuclei with localized DAF-16::GFP after 18 hr exposure to either OP50-1 or PA14 following acute heat shock. ** t-test, p<0.001 (F-H) Proportion of worms in a population categorized as either showing predominately nuclear localized ("nuclear") or predominately "delocalized" intestinal DAF-16::GFP. Nuclear localization was induced by either heat shock (70-90 minutes at 37degreesC) (F) or loss of germline proliferation (G-H) and then worms were exposed to (F-H) OP50-1, PA14, PA14 gacA, (G) SL1344, V583, (H) PA14 lasR, or PA14 rhlR. *** Fisher's exact test, p<0.0001.
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 433 437 433 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lin1">[68]</xref>
###xml 457 465 457 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdc-25.1</italic>
###xml 514 518 514 518 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira2">[76]</xref>
###xml 645 650 645 650 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">kri-1</italic>
###xml 650 654 650 654 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Berman1">[77]</xref>
###xml 687 695 687 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdc-25.1</italic>
###xml 867 872 867 872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">kri-1</italic>
###xml 899 908 899 908 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s009">Figure S8</xref>
###xml 1110 1114 1110 1114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1148 1157 1148 1157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4G</xref>
###xml 90 94 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 222 226 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 958 962 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1105 1109 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1195 1199 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1663 1667 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1752 1756 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1914 1918 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2108 2112 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2189 2193 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
To confirm that the rapid delocalization of DAF-16 is a general physiological response to PA14 infection and not an artifact specific to the use of heat shock stimulus to nuclear localize DAF-16, we examined the effect of PA14 infection on nuclear localized DAF-16 using worms in which germline proliferation was eliminated. Loss of germline proliferation causes nuclear localization of DAF-16 in the intestinal cells of adult worms [68]. RNAi knockdown of cdc-25.1 produces worms that lack germline proliferation [76] and localizes DAF-16::GFP to intestinal nuclei. Nuclear localization of DAF-16 due to loss of germline proliferation requires kri-1[77]. We confirmed that knockdown of cdc-25.1 by RNAi affects DAF-16::GFP nuclear localization through its effect on germline proliferation by showing that nuclear localization of DAF-16::GFP could be suppressed when kri-1 was knocked down by RNAi (Figure S8). In adult worms without proliferating germline, PA14 infection caused delocalization of nuclear DAF-16 in approximately 75% of worms after 16 hours (p<0.0001), whereas worms exposed to OP50-1 or PA14 gacA were not significantly affected (Figure 4G). Delocalization of DAF-16::GFP upon PA14 infection was not due to a generalized loss of nuclear localization because we failed to observe a loss of nuclear integrity. Nor was it due to a loss of the ability to retain transcription factors in the nucleus because other nuclear localized GFP constructs, including a translational fusion of GFP to the GATA transcription factor ELT-2, remained nuclear over the course of the experiment (data not shown). In addition, DAF-16 nuclear delocalization caused by PA14 infection was reversible by subsequent heat shock (data not shown), indicating that PA14 infection does not simply render DAF-16 incapable of nuclear translocation or retention. Notably, the nuclear delocalization of DAF-16 occurred early during PA14 infection and affected DAF-16 in intestinal nuclei. Thus, delocalization of DAF-16 occurred in the appropriate time and location to account for the transcriptional patterns observed during PA14 infection, providing an independent category of evidence for the model that PA14 infection activates the DAF-2 insulin-like signaling pathway.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 62 75 62 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 95 106 95 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. faecalis</italic>
###xml 117 131 117 131 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 142 151 142 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 732 741 732 741 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 846 855 846 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4G</xref>
###xml 903 907 903 907 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 909 913 909 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 919 923 919 923 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 996 1005 996 1005 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1C</xref>
###xml 1028 1032 1028 1032 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1045 1049 1045 1049 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 1054 1058 1054 1058 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1163 1172 1163 1172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4H</xref>
###xml 1328 1351 1328 1351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1</italic>
###xml 1393 1406 1393 1406 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 62 75 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 77 81 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 95 106 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 108 112 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">V583</span>
###xml 117 131 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 200 204 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">V583</span>
###xml 311 315 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">V583</span>
###xml 351 355 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 420 424 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">V583</span>
###xml 460 464 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 679 683 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">V583</span>
###xml 980 984 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1023 1027 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1393 1406 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
DAF-16 target genes were downregulated following infection by P. aeruginosa (PA14), but not by E. faecalis (V583) or S. typhimurium (SL1344) (Figure 1A). We therefore hypothesized that infection with V583 and SL1344 would not result in the translocation of DAF-16 from the nucleus. Because survival of worms on V583 and SL1344 is extended compared to PA14, delocalization of DAF-16 might occur later in worms exposed to V583 or SL1344 than in worms exposed to PA14. We therefore used worms lacking a proliferating germline to cause DAF-16 nuclear localization to ensure that nuclear localization of DAF-16 is distinguishable for at least 96 hours. Consistent with the failure of V583 and SL1344 to downregulate DAF-16 target genes (Figure 1A), there was no significant decrease in DAF-16 nuclear localization in worms exposed to these pathogens (Figure 4G). Finally, consistent with the requirement for gacA, lasR, and rhlR for the downregulation of immune gene expression during PA14 infection (Figure 1C), similar to the PA14 gacA mutant, the rhlR and lasR mutants also failed to cause significant delocalization of DAF-16::GFP compared to uninfected controls (Figure 4H). Thus, we can conclude that activation of DAF-2 affects the nuclear localization of DAF-16 and the transcription of DAF-2-dependent immune genes, such as thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1. This effect is specific to infection by P. aeruginosa and requires GacA-, LasR-, and RhlR-regulated virulence factors.
###end p 45
###begin title 46
###xml 51 64 51 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 51 64 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
DAF-2 and a DAF-2 agonist, INS-7, are required for P. aeruginosa to affect DAF-16 nuclear localization
###end title 46
###begin p 47
###xml 253 258 253 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 357 369 357 369 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 575 584 575 584 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 607 612 607 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 762 774 762 774 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 827 837 827 837 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 911 916 911 916 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 45 49 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 429 433 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 510 514 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 665 669 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 718 722 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 801 805 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 827 837 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The results presented thus far indicate that PA14 infection activates DAF-2, resulting in the translocation of DAF-16 from the nucleus and the DAF-2-dependent repression of immune gene expression. They further suggest that loss-of-function mutations in daf-2 would suppress the delocalization of DAF-16. Indeed, when we compared DAF-16::GFP localization in daf-2(e1370); DAF-16::GFP animals that were exposed to either OP50-1 or PA14, no significant difference in DAF-16::GFP localization was observed between PA14-infected and uninfected controls over the course of 4 days (Figure 5A). This indicates that daf-2 is required for the delocalization of DAF-16 during PA14 infection and is consistent with the failure of PA14 to downregulate host effector genes in daf-2(e1370). It further suggests that PA14 infection suppresses C. elegans immune gene expression by affecting host components that are upstream of daf-2.
###end p 47
###begin title 48
###xml 83 96 83 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 83 96 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Insulin-like signaling is required for the delocalization of nuclear DAF-16 during P. aeruginosa infection.
###end title 48

###xml 1097 1111 1097 1111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-11(tm1053)</italic>
###xml 1195 1204 1195 1204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s010">Figure S9</xref>
###xml 1206 1214 1206 1214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s014">Table S3</xref>
###xml 1243 1248 1243 1248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 1331 1337 1331 1337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-11</italic>
###xml 1384 1393 1384 1393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 1412 1417 1412 1417 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 1537 1550 1537 1550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7(tm1907)</italic>
###xml 1560 1565 1560 1565 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 1680 1689 1680 1689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g005">Figure 5D</xref>
###xml 1708 1713 1708 1713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 83 93 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 251 264 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 389 393 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 502 506 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 579 590 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 594 608 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 658 669 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 730 734 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 950 954 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 963 974 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 1050 1054 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1189 1193 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1274 1278 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1448 1452 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1591 1595 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1744 1748 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
daf-2 encodes the only homolog of a mammalian insulin/IGF-1-family receptor in the C. elegans genome [78], and its activity is affected by insulin-like molecules [79],[80]. Therefore, insulin-like peptides are attractive candidates to be subverted by P. aeruginosa to activate DAF-2. As shown in Figure 5B, two insulin-like peptides, ins-7 and ins-11, were upregulated in worms exposed to PA14. Several lines of evidence implicate ins-7-and not ins-11-as contributing to the activation of DAF-2 during PA14 infection. First, ins-7 expression is not induced by exposure to either E. faecalis or S. typhimurium, but ins-11 expression is induced by exposure to E. faecalis (Figure 5B). Also, ins-7 is not induced in worms exposed to PA14 gacA, lasR, or rhlR mutants (Figure 5B and unpublished data). Moreover, ins-7 is known to be an insulin agonist [16],[80]. Thus, the induction of ins-7, but not ins-11, is concordant with the activation of DAF-2 by PA14 but not E. faecalis infection. Second, the ins-7 deletion mutant ins-7(tm1907) is resistant to PA14 infection, but the ins-11 deletion mutant ins-11(tm1053) is not distinguishable from wildtype worms with respect to susceptibility to PA14 (Figure S9, Table S3). Lastly, RNAi knockdown of ins-7 suppresses the effect of PA14 infection on DAF-16 nuclear delocalization, whereas ins-11 RNAi knockdown has no distinguishable effect (Figure 5C). To confirm that ins-7 is required for the effect of PA14 on DAF-16 localization, we examined DAF-16::GFP localization in the deletion mutant ins-7(tm1907). Loss of ins-7 suppressed the effect of PA14 infection on DAF-16 nuclear delocalization in worms lacking germline proliferation (Figure 5D), indicating that ins-7 is required for the effect of PA14 on DAF-16 nuclear localization.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
###xml 56 60 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
DAF-16 is required in the intestine for defense against PA14
###end title 51

###xml 1983 1987 1983 1987 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-LorinNebel1">[85]</xref>
###xml 2054 2062 2054 2062 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s015">Table S4</xref>
###xml 2100 2103 2100 2103 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 2104 2108 2104 2108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Garsin1">[15]</xref>
###xml 2109 2113 2109 2113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kerry1">[23]</xref>
###xml 2114 2118 2114 2118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Miyata2">[81]</xref>
###xml 2138 2144 2138 2144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 2207 2216 2207 2216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g006">Figure 6A</xref>
###xml 2237 2243 2237 2243 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 2309 2318 2309 2318 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g006">Figure 6B</xref>
###xml 2508 2514 2508 2514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-22</italic>
###xml 2670 2674 2670 2674 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Waterston1">[86]</xref>
###xml 2702 2708 2702 2708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-22</italic>
###xml 2790 2796 2790 2796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-22</italic>
###xml 2878 2886 2878 2886 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s015">Table S4</xref>
###xml 2995 2999 2995 2999 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Pujol3">[87]</xref>
###xml 3105 3111 3105 3111 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 3171 3179 3171 3179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s015">Table S4</xref>
###xml 388 392 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 682 686 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 815 819 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 977 981 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1126 1130 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1399 1403 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1641 1651 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 2048 2052 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2201 2205 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2303 2307 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 3264 3268 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 3445 3449 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 3543 3547 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
daf-16 null mutants are indistinguishable from wildtype in their ability to survive infection by a variety of pathogens [8],[15],[23],[81]. However, the phenotype that results from the loss of gene function in an entire organism is the combination of the effects on various tissues; and the tissue required for daf-16 in immune function has not been investigated. The profound effects of PA14 infection on insulin-like signaling, and the central role for DAF-16 in that interaction, led us to reevaluate the role of DAF-16 in defense against bacterial pathogens. Several lines of evidence suggested an important role for DAF-16 in the intestine. First, the intestine is the site of PA14 infection [82], and the major site of expression of host defense genes including spp-1 and lys-7[7],[39]. Second, resistance to PA14 is associated with nuclear localization of DAF-16 specifically in the intestine. Loss of germline proliferation, which causes DAF-16-dependent resistance to PA14 (unpublished data), causes DAF-16 nuclear localization predominately in the intestine [68]. A forward genetic screen for enhanced resistance to PA14 identified mutants with enhanced nuclear localization of DAF-16 in the intestine [81]. Similarly, we have observed that loss of ins-7 caused DAF-16::GFP nuclear localization primarily in intestinal cells (unpublished data). Third, DAF-16 nuclear delocalization during PA14 infection is most evident in intestinal cells. Thus, we sought to examine the function of intestinal DAF-16 by knocking down the expression of daf-16 only in the intestine. Tissue-specific knockdown of gene expression can be achieved in C. elegans using strains in which the RNAi-deficient rde-1 mutant is rescued by expressing a transgene carrying the rde-1 gene in a specific tissue, such as intestine [83], hypodermis or muscle [84]. The strain VP303 expresses rde-1 in the intestine of an rde-1(ne219) mutant background, allowing for intestine-restricted RNAi knockdown [83],[85]. VP303 and N2 worms are indistinguishable for resistance to PA14 (Table S4). As expected from previous reports, [8],[15],[23],[81], RNAi knockdown of daf-16 in wildtype N2 worms had no effect on susceptibility to PA14 (Figure 6A). RNAi knockdown of daf-16 in VP303 worms, however, caused enhanced susceptibility to PA14 (Figure 6B). To confirm the specificity of VP303 for intestine-specific knockdown, we exposed N2 and VP303 strains to bacteria that express double-stranded RNA corresponding to a muscle-specific gene unc-22, which encodes for twitchin that functions in the muscles to regulate the actomyosin contraction-relaxation cycle and to maintain normal muscle morphology [86]. As expected, RNAi against unc-22 resulted in the canonical twitching phenotype in N2 but not in the VP303 strain. unc-22 RNAi also has no effect on pathogen resistance in both the N2 and VP303 strains (Table S4). Recently, the hypodermal tissue has also been shown to contribute to immune response to a fungal pathogen [87]. Using the NR222 strain, in which RNAi knockdown is restricted to the hypodermis, we showed that loss of daf-16 in the hypodermis is not required for pathogen resistance (Table S4). These results indicate that DAF-16 is required in the intestine for resistance to PA14, whereas loss of DAF-16 in the intestine, in combination with loss of DAF-16 in non-intestinal tissues, has an overall neutral effect on the ability of worms to defend against PA14 infection. Intestinally but not hypodermally expressed DAF-16 is essential for resistance to PA14, a function that was previously masked in studies examining the requirement for DAF-16 in the whole worm.
###end p 52
###begin title 53
###xml 61 74 61 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 61 74 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Intestinal DAF-16 is specifically required for resistance to P. aeruginosa.
###end title 53
###begin p 54
###xml 157 163 151 157 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 286 292 280 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 36 40 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 324 328 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
(A-B) Survival of worms cultured on PA14 lawns was monitored over time at 25degreesC. (A) In wildtype N2 worms, the effects on survival of RNAi knockdown of daf-16 or control RNAi were indistinguishable (logrank, p = 0.85). (B) In VP303 worms, intestinally restricted RNAi knockdown of daf-16 caused enhanced sensitivity to PA14 compared to control RNAi (logrank, p = 0.0002).
###end p 54

Pseudomonas infection suppresses host defense genes
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 318 323 318 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
