###xml 1174 1188 1174 1188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 1190 1199 1190 1199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 1397 1406 1397 1406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1B</xref>
###xml 1411 1419 1411 1419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s013">Table S2</xref>
###xml 1548 1561 1548 1561 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 1566 1576 1566 1576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 1630 1634 1630 1634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1636 1640 1636 1640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1645 1649 1645 1649 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 1682 1691 1682 1691 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1C</xref>
###xml 1694 1698 1694 1698 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1700 1704 1700 1704 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 1709 1713 1709 1713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 1756 1764 1756 1764 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s012">Table S1</xref>
###xml 2111 2121 2111 2121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 2266 2276 2266 2276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA, pqsA</italic>
###xml 2415 2419 2415 2419 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Bleves1">[49]</xref>
###xml 2421 2425 2421 2425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Yahr1">[50]</xref>
###xml 2427 2431 2427 2431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kay1">[52]</xref>
###xml 2432 2436 2432 2436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wade1">[54]</xref>
###xml 2480 2485 2480 2485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 2498 2508 2498 2508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 2668 2678 2668 2678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 2733 2737 2729 2733 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Apidianakis1">[36]</xref>
###xml 2784 2794 2780 2790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 2796 2806 2792 2802 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s004">Figure S3B</xref>
###xml 2859 2872 2855 2868 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 2885 2895 2881 2891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 367 371 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 507 511 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 703 707 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 758 762 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 958 962 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1044 1054 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1158 1169 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 1174 1188 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 1282 1286 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1489 1493 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1548 1561 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1566 1576 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 1585 1589 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2668 2678 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila</span>
###xml 2784 2794 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 2859 2872 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 2885 2895 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Models of host-pathogen interactions predict that pathogen challenge will result in the induction of host defense genes. Repression of host defense genes is often associated with suppression of host defense pathways by the pathogen. Using quantitative RT-PCR, we confirmed that known host defense effectors, including thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 are downregulated during PA14 infection (Figure 1A). Because knockdown of basal expression of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 by RNAi resulted in enhanced susceptibility to PA14 (Figure S1), suppression of their expression during infection should compromise host defense. The observation that knockdown of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 by RNAi causes enhanced sensitivity to PA14 despite the downregulation of their expression in PA14-infected worms is explained in part by the fact that expression levels drop following infection whereas expression levels are already reduced to low levels when RNAi-treated worms are exposed to PA14. The downregulation of these host defense effectors is not a typical response of C. elegans to pathogen challenge; the expression of these host effectors was induced or unaffected in response to E. faecalis and S. typhimurium (Figure 1A). A large number of host defense effectors are efficiently induced in response to PA14 infection, suggesting that the downregulation of a particular set of host defense genes is a specific effect (Figure 1B and Table S2). Also, repression of a specific subset of host defense effectors by PA14 is likely to represent a specific interaction between P. aeruginosa and C. elegans because PA14 requires the virulence regulatory genes gacA, lasR and rhlR to suppress host defense genes (Figure 1C). gacA, lasR and rhlR mutants are each attenuated in virulence (Table S1), suggesting a link between virulence and the downregulation of host defense effectors. The specific requirement of GacA-, LasR- and RhlR-regulated virulence factors in immune suppression is supported by the observation that the PA14_23420, PA14_23430, PA14_59010 mutants that are attenuated in virulence are not defective in immune suppression (Figure S3B). As an initial effort to define the GacA-, LasR- and RhlR-regulated virulence factors that are required for immune suppression, we showed that dsbA, pqsA and the T3SS, all of which have been shown to be under the control of the GacS/GacA two component regulator and the quorum-sensing system [49], [50], [52]-[54] are not required for the downregulation of lys-7 expression (Figure S3B). The hypothetical protein, PA14_41070 that contains the S-adenosyl-methionine (SAM)-dependent methyltransferase domain that is required for downregulation of Drosophila NF-kappaB-regulated antimicrobial peptides expression [36] is also dispensable for immune suppression in C. elegans (Figure S3B). Overall these results suggest that the ability of P. aeruginosa to suppress C. elegans host defense effectors requires a subset of GacA-, LasR- and RhlR-regulated virulence factors and are not merely reflections of attenuation of virulence.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 320 324 316 320 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Apidianakis1">[36]</xref>
###xml 325 329 321 325 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Grant1">[43]</xref>
###xml 330 334 326 330 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Angot1">[44]</xref>
###xml 635 648 631 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 635 648 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
We have thus provided evidence that we have identified a new mechanism of host immune suppression. This mechanism does not require the SAM-dependent methyltransfrease or the type III secretion system, which have been previously implicated in host immune suppression through their effects on NF-kappaB and MAPK signaling [36],[43],[44]. Instead, it requires the GacA two-component regulator and the LasR and RhlR quorum-sensing regulators to regulate factors necessary to subvert host defense. These factors, which we showed are likely to be independent of DsbA and quinolone signaling, could potentially be identified by screening for P. aeruginosa mutants that fail to downregulate the expression of host defense effectors, a strategy that we are actively pursuing. Finally, as discussed below, this immune suppression is mediated by the host insulin-like signaling pathway, instead of the MAPK and NF-kappaB pathways.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 0 11 0 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
Pseudomonas infection activates insulin-like signaling
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 58 81 58 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1</italic>
###xml 89 102 89 102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 114 123 114 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1A</xref>
###xml 196 209 196 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 451 459 451 459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 484 507 484 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1</italic>
###xml 547 552 547 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 579 591 579 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3A&#8211;3C</xref>
###xml 614 619 614 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 762 771 762 771 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2A</xref>
###xml 872 881 872 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2C</xref>
###xml 1112 1124 1109 1121 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1272 1284 1266 1278 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2C&#8211;2E</xref>
###xml 89 102 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 196 209 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 311 315 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 515 519 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1175 1179 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
The specific downregulation of the host defense effectors thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 during P. aeruginosa infection (Figure 1A) suggested that a host defense signaling pathway was being subverted by P. aeruginosa to repress host defenses. Gene expression and host protein localization studies support a model that PA14 infection activates the DAF-2/DAF-16 insulin-like signaling pathway, resulting in the downregulation of DAF-16-regulated immune genes (Figure 7). The downregulation of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 during PA14 infection was abolished in daf-2 loss-of-function mutants (Figure 3A-3C). The requirement for daf-2 for gene downregulation during infection held true when the gene expression analysis was extended to include the entire genome by microarray (Figure 2A) or to a set of 146 candidate immune and stress genes that were measured more precisely by qRT-PCR (Figure 2C). Comparison of the transcriptional response to infection in mutants of each of the p38 MAPK, Sma/TGF-beta, and insulin-like signaling pathways to the response in wildtype N2 worms confirms that the insulin-like signaling mutant, daf-2(e1370), suppresses a portion of the wildtype response to PA14 infection in a fashion distinct from the effects of loss of p38 MAPK or TGF-beta signaling (Figure 2C-2E).
###end p 60
###begin title 61
###xml 9 22 9 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 9 22 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
Model of P. aeruginosa activation of insulin-like signaling.
###end title 61
###begin p 62
###xml 107 112 107 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 431 436 431 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 441 446 441 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 687 692 687 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 527 531 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
PA14 infection causes an insulin agonist-mediated activation of DAF-2, which likely involves expression of ins-7. Upon DAF-2 activation, several serine-threonine kinases phorphorylate DAF-16, causing the transcription factor to be retained in the cytoplasm and inhibiting its transcriptional-regulatory activity. Consequently, DAF-2-regulated gene expression is affected, causing the downregulation of immune defense genes such as lys-7 and thn-2. Germline signaling and heat shock regulate DAF-16 in parallel to the effect of PA14 and DAF-2 activity. DAF-2 and DAF-16 may function in a network with other signaling components to affect the expression of DAF-2-regulated genes including spp-1.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 24 32 24 32 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 362 366 362 366 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lin1">[68]</xref>
###xml 367 371 367 371 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Henderson1">[73]</xref>
###xml 552 560 552 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 607 615 607 615 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g001">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 757 768 757 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. faecalis</italic>
###xml 772 786 772 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 813 817 813 817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 819 823 819 823 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 828 832 828 832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>
###xml 969 981 969 981 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g004">Figure 4G&#8211;4H</xref>
###xml 1482 1494 1482 1494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 1531 1540 1531 1540 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g005">Figure 5A</xref>
###xml 1604 1615 1604 1615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. faecalis</italic>
###xml 1617 1631 1617 1631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 1641 1645 1641 1645 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 1702 1707 1702 1707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 1725 1730 1725 1730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 1772 1777 1772 1777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2</italic>
###xml 1809 1818 1809 1818 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g005">Figure 5B</xref>
###xml 1889 1894 1889 1894 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 1969 1978 1969 1978 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g005">Figure 5C</xref>
###xml 2102 2107 2102 2107 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 54 58 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 459 463 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 499 503 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 703 707 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 757 768 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 772 786 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 797 801 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1027 1031 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1211 1215 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1391 1395 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1515 1519 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1567 1571 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1604 1615 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 1617 1631 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 1636 1640 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1793 1797 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1921 1925 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2061 2065 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
The model we propose in Figure 7 predicts that during PA14 infection, activation of insulin-like signaling will result in the inhibition of DAF-16. Inhibition of DAF-16 by insulin-like signaling is mediated by phosophorylation of DAF-16 by serine threonine kinases that are homologous to mammalian AKT and SGK, and results in the cytoplasmic retention of DAF-16 [68],[73]. We used several assay conditions to examine the nuclear localization of DAF-16 during PA14 infection, providing evidence that PA14 infection causes DAF-16 nuclear delocalization (Figure 4). Based on the transcriptional response data (Figure 1), we further predicted that nuclear delocalization would occur in response to wildtype PA14, but would not occur in response to infection by E. faecalis or S. typhimurium, and that PA14 mutants of gacA, lasR and rhlR would also be defective for the ability to cause delocalization of nuclear DAF-16. Each of these predictions was confirmed when tested (Figure 4G-4H), suggesting that DAF-16 delocalization is a PA14-infection specific effect. The model also predicted that while stimuli that function in parallel to insulin-like signaling to cause DAF-16 nuclear localization can be reversed by PA14 infection, such as heat shock and loss of germline proliferation, mutations that disrupt insulin-like signaling would also disrupt the DAF-16 nuclear delocalization caused by PA14. We confirmed that nuclear localization of DAF-16 in the insulin-like receptor mutant daf-2(e1370) was not affected by PA14 infection (Figure 5A). Finally, we showed that PA14 infection, but not infection by E. faecalis, S. typhimurium, or PA14 gacA caused increased expression of the insulin-like peptide ins-7, suggesting that ins-7 may participate in signaling upstream of daf-2 in response to PA14 infection (Figure 5B). Consistent with this hypothesis, we found that a deletion mutant of ins-7 attenuated the ability of PA14 to cause nuclear delocalization of DAF-16 (Figure 5C). Collectively, the expression profile and DAF-16 localization data indicate that PA14 infection induces the expression of ins-7 to activate insulin signaling that leads to inhibition of DAF-16 and downregulation of immune gene expression.
###end p 63
###begin p 64
###xml 142 146 142 146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Apfeld1">[88]</xref>
###xml 147 151 147 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Ailion1">[89]</xref>
###xml 172 176 172 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Bargmann1">[90]</xref>
###xml 272 277 272 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 375 387 375 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-64(e246)</italic>
###xml 392 404 392 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-31(e928)</italic>
###xml 781 793 781 793 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">unc-64(e246)</italic>
###xml 1098 1103 1098 1103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 428 432 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 657 661 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 825 829 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1001 1005 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1057 1061 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
In a separate report, we showed that a neuroendrocine signaling axis that functions upstream of the DAF-2/DAF-16 pathway to regulate lifespan [88],[89] and dauer formation [90] also regulates innate immunity. Regulation of innate immunity is mediated by the expression of ins-7 in the neurons (unpublished data). We showed that mutants with decreased neurosecretion, such as unc-64(e246) and unc-31(e928), are more resistant to PA14 because they express significantly higher levels of immune effectors due to constitutive nuclear localization of intestinal DAF-16. In that report, we tested whether neuronal function was required for activation of DAF-2 by PA14 infection. We found that constitutive nuclear localization of DAF-16::GFP in neurosecretion defective mutants, such as unc-64(e246) is not reversed by exposure to PA14 (data not shown). Taken together, the data indicate neuronal secretion of an insulin-like peptide, INS-7, contributes to activation of DAF-2 insulin-like signaling during PA14 infection. It will be interesting to determine how PA14 infection induces the expression of ins-7 in neurons and thereby suppress immune gene expression.
###end p 64
###begin title 65
###xml 54 65 54 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pseudomonas</italic>
Other contributors to the transcriptional response to Pseudomonas
###end title 65
###begin p 66
###xml 201 217 201 217 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2A and 2C</xref>
###xml 419 434 416 431 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g002">Figure 2B,2D,2E</xref>
###xml 541 549 538 546 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s013">Table S2</xref>
###xml 845 849 842 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-He1">[91]</xref>
###xml 119 123 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 413 417 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 485 489 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 622 626 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 732 736 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Activation of DAF-2 appears to account for a substantial proportion of the downregulation of host defense genes during PA14 infection, but is less important for the upregulation of host defense genes (Figure 2A and 2C). To understand the mechanisms contributing to gene upregulation during infection, we also examined the contributions of the Sma/TGF-beta and p38 MAPK pathways to the transcriptional response to PA14 (Figure 2B,2D,2E). For many genes, the transcriptional response to PA14 is intact in mutants of all three pathways tested (Table S2). This indicates that the regulation of the transcriptional response to PA14 is redundant and/or that additional pathways contribute substantially to the transcriptional response to PA14. Functional redundancy in the regulation of host immune effectors is a conserved feature of innate immunity [91]. In light of this observation, it is especially notable that the downregulation of a substantial number of genes is dependent on DAF-2 insulin-like signaling.
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 19 24 19 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 34 43 34 43 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3C</xref>
###xml 72 77 72 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 82 87 82 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 89 105 89 105 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g003">Figure 3A and 3B</xref>
###xml 298 303 295 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 305 314 302 311 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s005">Figure S4</xref>
###xml 319 327 316 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s013">Table S2</xref>
###xml 383 388 380 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 471 479 468 476 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="ppat-1000175-g007">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 28 32 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
The suppression of spp-1 by PA14 (Figure 3C), unlike the suppression of thn-2 and lys-7 (Figure 3A and 3B), is not entirely DAF-16 dependent, suggesting additional layers of complexity in the regulation of DAF-2 target genes. Neither p38 MAPK nor Sma/TGF-beta is required for the downregulation of spp-1 (Figure S4 and Table S2). The factor that contributes to the downregulation of spp-1 remains unknown, but may function downstream of DAF-2 in cooperation with DAF-16 (Figure 7).
###end p 67
###begin p 68
###xml 136 140 136 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Hsu1">[75]</xref>
###xml 141 145 141 145 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wolff1">[92]</xref>
###xml 146 150 146 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Tullet1">[93]</xref>
###xml 281 286 281 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">elt-2</italic>
###xml 406 409 406 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 438 448 438 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 477 480 477 480 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 481 485 481 485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kerry1">[23]</xref>
###xml 751 755 751 755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Murphy1">[16]</xref>
###xml 920 933 920 933 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>

###xml 1051 1056 1051 1056 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1062 1067 1062 1067 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sod-3</italic>
###xml 1201 1209 1201 1209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 1209 1213 1209 1213 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Furuyama1">[70]</xref>
###xml 1272 1277 1272 1277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1282 1287 1282 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sod-3</italic>
###xml 1297 1302 1297 1302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1304 1309 1304 1309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>

###xml 1384 1389 1384 1389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 1394 1399 1394 1399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 1489 1494 1489 1494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 1517 1520 1517 1520 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 2022 2026 2022 2026 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Tullet1">[93]</xref>
###xml 2058 2063 2058 2063 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">skn-1</italic>
###xml 2299 2304 2299 2304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">skn-1</italic>
###xml 2351 2356 2351 2356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 2358 2363 2358 2363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2368 2373 2368 2373 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 2392 2397 2392 2397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 2444 2449 2444 2449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 2451 2456 2451 2456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 2462 2467 2462 2467 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 2482 2487 2482 2487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">skn-1</italic>
###xml 2546 2551 2546 2551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 2628 2633 2628 2633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gst-4</italic>
###xml 2646 2656 2646 2656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s008">Figure S7C</xref>
###xml 401 405 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 438 448 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 920 933 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 1502 1506 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1906 1910 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2137 2141 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2270 2274 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 2562 2566 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
A number of transcriptional co-regulators have been identified which regulate lifespan and stress resistance in conjunction with DAF-16 [75],[92],[93]. We considered two transcription factors, ELT-2 and SKN-1, as likely candidates because they are also expressed in the intestine. elt-2 encodes a GATA transcription factor that is required for a substantial portion of the transcriptional response to PA14 [7], and is required to protect C. elegans from infection by pathogens [7],[23]. However, the pathways that act upstream of ELT-2 in the regulation of immune defense has not be elucidated. Intriguingly, a CTTATCA (reverse complement: TGATAAG) DNA motif that is enriched in the 5-prime flanking regions (5'-flank) of DAF-2/DAF-16-regulated genes [16] is essentially identical to a GATA-like motif (TGATAAGA) that is enriched in the 5'-flank of genes that are significantly up- or down-regulated in worms exposed to P. aeruginosa[7], and each is a derivative of the consensus GATA motif (WGATAR). For example, the 5'-flank of spp-1, thn-2, gst-4, lys-7, and sod-3 each contain GATA motifs. This motif is distinct from the canonical FOXO binding site (TRTTTAG), which has been shown to bind DAF-16 in vitro[70]. The FOXO-binding DNA motif is present in the 5'-flank of lys-7 and sod-3, but not spp-1, thn-2, or gst-4. Moreover, knockdown of elt-2 by RNAi reduces the expression of lys-7 and spp-1 under uninfected conditions (data not shown) and enhances the relative downregulation of thn-2 during PA14 infection [7]. Overall, these findings suggest that ELT-2 or another GATA-motif-binding transcription factor may function downstream of DAF-2 together with DAF-16 to regulate the expression of immune-response gene. One instantiation of the consensus-binding motif of the transcription factor SKN-1 (ATGATAAT) is remarkably similar to the WGATAR motifs found upstream of genes regulated by DAF-2 and PA14 infection. Recently, it has recently been shown that for lifespan SKN-1 is regulated by insulin-like signaling [93]. We observed that knockdown of skn-1 by RNAi throughout the life of the animal caused enhanced sensitivity to PA14 (unpublished data). Thus, we wondered whether SKN-1 might contribute to DAF-2-dependent regulation of gene expression following PA14 infection. Knockdown of skn-1 by RNAi does not affect the downregulation of thn-2, spp-1, or lys-7 (data not shown). gst-4 is known to be SKN-1-regulated. However, like thn-2, spp-1, and lys-7, knockdown of skn-1 expression by RNAi does not abolish the downregulation of gst-4 following PA14 infection, despite causing a reduction in the basal level of gst-4 expression (Figure S7C). Future work must focus on determining transcription factors in addition to DAF-16 that accounts for the DAF-2-dependent downregulation of host defense genes.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 132 138 132 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acdh-1</italic>
###xml 214 226 214 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 228 236 228 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s013">Table S2</xref>
###xml 425 431 422 428 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acdh-1</italic>
###xml 485 558 482 555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. faecalis, E. carotovora, P. luminescens, S. marcescens, S. typhimurium</italic>
###xml 568 572 565 569 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 625 629 622 626 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wong1">[21]</xref>
###xml 670 676 667 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">acdh-1</italic>
###xml 116 120 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 400 404 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 485 496 <span type="species:ncbi:1351">E. faecalis</span>
###xml 498 511 <span type="species:ncbi:554">E. carotovora</span>
###xml 513 527 <span type="species:ncbi:29488">P. luminescens</span>
###xml 529 542 <span type="species:ncbi:615">S. marcescens</span>
###xml 544 558 <span type="species:ncbi:90371">S. typhimurium</span>
###xml 563 567 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
We also note that not every downregulated gene is dependent on DAF-2 insulin-like signaling. For example, following PA14 infection, acdh-1 is strongly repressed in wildtype and all of the mutants tested, including daf-2(e1370) (Table S2). This suggests that factors in addition to DAF-2 insulin-like, Sma/TGF-beta, and p38 MAPK signaling may contribute to the repression of host defense genes during PA14 infection. However, acdh-1 expression is also downregulated in worms exposed to E. faecalis, E. carotovora, P. luminescens, S. marcescens, S. typhimurium and PA14 gacA (M. Nandakumar and M.-W. Tan, unpublished data, and [21]), suggesting that the downregulation of acdh-1 may represent a different phenomena than the repression of other host defense genes.
###end p 69
###begin title 70
Insulin-like signaling regulates intestinal immune defense
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 171 177 171 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 309 312 309 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Troemel1">[8]</xref>
###xml 313 317 313 317 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Garsin1">[15]</xref>
###xml 318 322 318 322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Kerry1">[23]</xref>
###xml 323 327 323 327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Miyata2">[81]</xref>
###xml 343 349 343 349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 411 423 411 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16(mu86)</italic>
###xml 424 436 424 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 889 895 889 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 942 948 942 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 1122 1127 1122 1127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 646 650 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1131 1135 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Given the dynamic regulation of insulin-like signaling during infection, and particularly the complex role for DAF-16 in this interaction, we wondered why null mutants of daf-16 are nonetheless indistinguishable from wildtype animals for their ability to survive infection by a variety of bacterial pathogens [8],[15],[23],[81]. Expression of daf-16 in the intestine partially enhanced pathogen resistance of a daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370) worm (unpublished data), consistent with the intestine being the site of infection, and the major site of immune gene expression. Additional observations that germline signaling, neuroendocrine signaling, and PA14 infection primarily modulate DAF-16 nuclear localization in the intestine highlighted the importance of intestinal DAF-16. A compensatory mechanism or other complex interaction acting across tissues could potentially mask the function of daf-16 in the intestine. Using of intestine-specific daf-16 knockdown by RNAi we show that DAF-16 is required for a protective response against pathogen. Supporting this finding further is the observation that enhanced resistance of ins-7 to PA14 is associated with constitutive nuclear localization of DAF-16 specifically in the intestine (unpublished data).
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 100 106 100 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 412 422 412 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 817 821 817 821 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-ArantesOliveira1">[94]</xref>
###xml 989 995 989 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 1072 1078 1072 1078 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 412 422 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
The most parsimonious explanation for the failure to observe enhanced sensitivity to pathogens when daf-16 is knocked down or knocked out in the whole organism is that intestinal and non-intestinal DAF-16 have antagonistic effects on host defense. Given the known complex regulation of DAF-16, this scenario is plausible. Balanced antagonistic effects on DAF-16 are observed in the context of signaling from the C. elegans germline and somatic gonad that regulate aging. Signals from the germline that normally suppress DAF-16 activity are balanced by distinct signals from the somatic gonad that normally enhance DAF-16 activity. The gonad signal appears to operate via the neurons and DAF-2 insulin-like signaling, while the germline signal appears to operate through a parallel pathway that does not require DAF-2 [94]. In this context, it is most appropriate to describe the effects of genetic manipulations in terms of net aggregate effects. Thus, the net aggregate effect of loss of daf-16 in the entire organism is neutral while the net aggregate effect of loss of daf-16 in the intestine results in pathogen sensitivity.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 135 145 135 145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 188 191 188 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 211 224 211 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 418 422 418 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Greer1">[95]</xref>
###xml 457 470 457 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 563 567 563 567 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Saiman1">[25]</xref>
###xml 568 572 568 572 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Lyczak1">[26]</xref>
###xml 709 722 709 722 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 135 145 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 160 165 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 211 224 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 457 470 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 503 511 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 709 722 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 758 763 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 764 772 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
Endodermal GATA transcription factors have been shown to have a conserved role in regulating epithelial innate immune responses in the C. elegans intestine and human lung epithelial cells [7]. Here we find that P. aeruginosa can suppress epithelial immunity by affecting DAF-16 activity in the intestinal cells. The regulation of FOXO/DAF-16 by insulin-like signaling is highly conserved across organisms (reviewed in [95]). Given the medical importance of P. aeruginosa, for example in cystic fibrosis patients where it chronically infects lung epithelial cells [25],[26], it will be interesting in the future to investigate whether insulin-like signaling regulates an epithelial immune response and whether P. aeruginosa suppresses this immune response in human patients.
###end p 73
###begin title 74
Materials and Methods
###end title 74
###begin title 75
Worm and bacterial strains
###end title 75
###begin p 76
###xml 0 22 0 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Caenorhabditis elegans</italic>
###xml 62 70 62 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s016">Table S5</xref>
###xml 162 166 162 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Brenner1">[96]</xref>
###xml 211 217 211 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-16</italic>
###xml 219 224 219 224 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 226 231 226 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn-2</italic>
###xml 237 242 237 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 257 267 257 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 294 301 294 301 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 377 382 377 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sod-3</italic>
###xml 384 389 384 389 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7</italic>
###xml 391 397 391 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-11</italic>
###xml 399 404 399 404 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">kri-1</italic>
###xml 410 415 410 415 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">skn-1</italic>
###xml 431 441 431 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 468 475 468 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 0 22 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
###xml 257 267 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 294 301 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
###xml 431 441 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 468 475 <span type="species:ncbi:110766|species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Caenorhabditis elegans and bacterial strains are described in Table S5. Double mutants were constructed and verified using standard genetic and molecular methods [96]. Bacteria expressing dsRNA directed against daf-16, lys-7, thn-2, and spp-1 was part of a C. elegans RNAi library expressed in E. coli (Geneservice, Cambridge, U.K.). Bacteria expressing dsRNA directed against sod-3, ins-7, ins-11, kri-1, and skn-1 were part of a C. elegans RNAi library expressed in E. coli (Open Biosystems, Huntsville, Alabama). All bacterial strains were cultured under standard conditions.
###end p 76
###begin title 77
Microarray analysis
###end title 77
###begin p 78
###xml 132 135 132 135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 287 297 287 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sma-6(wk7)</italic>
###xml 377 380 377 380 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 382 394 382 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">daf-2(e1370)</italic>
###xml 889 893 877 881 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Demeter1">[97]</xref>
###xml 246 250 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 519 523 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 1129 1133 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Growing worms for microarrays, RNA extraction, microarray hybridization, and data processing were performed as previously described [7]. Reference RNA and microarray hardware were matched to allow direct comparison of transcriptional response to PA14 in all worm strains. In particular, sma-6(wk7) experiments were performed in parallel with previously reported N2 experiments [7]. daf-2(e1370) animals were grown at 20degreesC until young adulthood and then placed for 24 hr at 25degreesC on lawns of either OP50-1 or PA14 grown on modified NGM. Microarray production, hybridization, and scanning were performed at the Stanford Functional Genomics Facility. cDNA was generated from total RNA. Experimental cDNA was labeled with Cy3 and reference cDNA was labeled with Cy5. Four replicates of each condition were examined. Microarray data was deposited in the Stanford Microarray Database [97]. The default background subtraction and normalization settings were used. Spots were filtered based on foreground to background ratio; values less than 1.2 were flagged. Log (base 2) values were exported. Gene expression on OP50-1 and PA14 were compared by t-test. Differences of 2 fold with p-values<0.05 were considered significant. Sensitivity analysis was conducted with a range of significance levels and fold-difference values to confirm that the choice of thresholds did not affect our conclusions.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
Quantitative RT-PCR
###end title 79
###begin p 80
###xml 188 191 188 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 600 605 586 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ama-1</italic>
###xml 631 640 617 626 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">act-1,3,4</italic>
###xml 75 79 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Age-matched young adult worms were exposed to bacterial lawns of OP50-1 or PA14 on NGM for 12 hours. RNA extraction and quantitative RT-PCR (qRT-PCR) was performed as previously described [7]. Briefly, 25 microl reactions were performed using the iScript One-Step RT-PCR kit with SYBR green according to the manufacturer's instructions (BioRad Laboratories, Hercules, CA), primers at a final concentration of 1 microM, and a data acquisition temperature of 76degreesC. In order to control for variation in RNA loading concentration, cycle threshold (Ct) values were normalized to three primer pairs (ama-1, F44B9.5, and pan-actin (act-1,3,4)) that were found to not change with infection. Summary statistics and statistical tests were calculated from N2-normalized cycle threshold values prior to conversion to relative fold change. Calculations were performed with a custom Perl script, Excel and R.
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 132 135 132 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">abf</italic>
###xml 149 152 149 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys</italic>
###xml 178 181 178 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp</italic>
###xml 205 208 205 208 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">thn</italic>
###xml 294 297 294 297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira1">[7]</xref>
###xml 329 333 329 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Murphy1">[16]</xref>
###xml 564 568 564 568 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Wrobel1">[98]</xref>
###xml 289 293 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
A panel of 146 infection and stress response genes queried by qRT-PCR included representatives of the antibacterial factor related (abf), lysozymes (lys), saposin-like proteins (spp), or thaumatin family (thn) gene classes, as well as genes identified to be transcriptionally regulated by PA14 [7] or by the DAF-2/DAF-16 pathway [16]. Whenever possible, primers were designed to amplify a sequence found in spliced cDNA but not genomic DNA by having one of the primer pairs overlap an exon junction. To this end, primer design was aided with the program AutoPrime [98]. Primer sequences are available from the authors upon request.
###end p 81
###begin title 82
###xml 50 54 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Analysis of induction and repression responses to PA14 infection
###end title 82
###begin p 83
###xml 186 187 186 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 305 306 305 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 348 349 348 349 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 348 349 348 349 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 444 445 444 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 535 536 535 536 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 534 536 534 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x<sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 543 544 543 544 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 543 544 543 544 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 551 552 551 552 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 601 602 601 602 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 647 648 647 648 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sub>
###xml 731 732 731 732 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x</sup>
###xml 731 732 731 732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sup>x</sup></italic>
###xml 754 755 754 755 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 753 755 753 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x<sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 761 762 761 762 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 761 762 761 762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 769 770 769 770 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 769 770 769 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 814 815 814 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 862 863 862 863 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 861 863 861 863 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x<sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 869 870 869 870 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 869 870 869 870 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 877 878 877 878 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 877 878 877 878 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 923 924 923 924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 150 154 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 327 331 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 497 501 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
To compare the response to infection in wildtype and mutant worms, RNA concentrations were measured in matched samples of worms exposed to OP50-1 and PA14. The RNA concentration of gene g in worms exposed to OP50-1 (designated OP50g) indicates the basal level of expression. The RNA concentration of gene g in worms exposed to PA14 (designated PA14g) indicates the level of expression that follows infection. The response to infection for gene g is the difference in RNA levels between OP50-1 and PA14 samples. This was quantified as xg = PA14g - OP50g for qRT-PCR cycle threshold measurements and log2-converted microarray measurements. These log2-scale values were interpreted as fold changes using the conversion fold change = 2x. Positive values of xg (PA14g - OP50g>0) indicate induction of the expression of g in response to infection. Negative values of xg (PA14g - OP50g<0) indicate repression of the expression of g in response to infection.
###end p 83
###begin p 84
###xml 19 20 19 20 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</sub>
###xml 18 20 18 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">x<sub>g</sub></italic>
###xml 163 169 163 169 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">strain</sub>
###xml 334 342 334 342 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wildtype</sub>
###xml 348 354 348 354 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mutant</sub>
###xml 357 358 357 358 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 460 461 460 461 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">2</sup>
###xml 285 289 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
An ordered set of xg values for a set of genes (such as the set of induced or the set of repressed genes) from a particular worm strain forms a vector designated Xstrain. Correlation analysis can be used to determine the effect of a mutation on the induction or repression response to PA14 infection. The squared correlation between Xwildtype and Xmutant, r2, indicates the degree to which induction or repression is conserved in the mutant strain. Values of r2 that are statistically indistinguishable from 0 indicate that induction or repression is strongly attenuated.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 32 40 32 40 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wildtype</sub>
###xml 46 52 46 52 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mutant</sub>
###xml 108 113 108 109 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 148 154 144 150 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">mutant</sub>
###xml 158 166 154 162 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">wildtype</sub>
###xml 169 174 165 166 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 345 350 337 338 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 411 416 399 400 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
###xml 477 482 461 462 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;</sub>
For a more sensitive analysis, Xwildtype and Xmutant were compared by paired t-test. The summary statistic XDelta was calculated as the average of Xmutant - Xwildtype. XDelta indicates both the magnitude and direction of the difference in induction or repression in response to infection between wildtype and mutant strains. For induced genes, XDelta<0 indicates attenuation of induction. For repressed genes, XDelta>0 indicates attenuation of repression. The significance of XDelta values was determined by paired t-test.
###end p 85
###begin title 86
DAF-16 nuclear localization assay
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 245 253 239 247 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdc-25.1</italic>
###xml 278 282 272 276 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira2">[76]</xref>
###xml 1434 1438 1426 1430 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Li1">[99]</xref>
###xml 311 315 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Acute heat shock was performed at 37degreesC for 70 to 90 minutes. Precise exposure times were determined empirically during each run by qualitative assessment of worms after heat shock. Germline proliferation was disrupted by RNAi knockdown of cdc-25.1 as previously described [76]. Worms were then exposed to PA14 or controls for approximately 16 hours; times varied from 14 to 18 hours as needed. Individual worms were classified as exhibiting predominantly nuclear DAF-16::GFP or predominantly delocalization DAF-16::GFP under 160x total magnification using an Olympus SZX12 dissecting microscope with a 1.6x objective and an EN GFP-LP filter cube (catalog no. 41018, Chroma Technology, Brattleboro, VT) which has the following specification: excitation band-pass filter 470+/-20 nm, emission filters >495 nm long pass followed by another >500 nm long pass. Fluorescence micrographs were collected at 200x magnification by fluorescence microscopy using a Leica DMRXA2 microscope with the Leica I3 filter set (Excitation 420 nm, Emission 525 nm, 30 nm band pass) for GFP. The criteria for predominately nuclear was the greater than 4 intestinal nuclei with nuclear localized DAF-16::GFP. The proportion of worms in each category is a metric for comparing the extent of nuclear localization of DAF-16 between populations, and have previously been used to examine the genetic control of DAF-16 nuclear localization in other contexts [99]. Assays scored in this fashion are highly reproducible between experiments and across experimenters.
###end p 87
###begin title 88
###xml 0 10 0 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 0 10 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
C. elegans survival assays
###end title 88
###begin p 89
###xml 35 45 35 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 100 104 100 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="ppat.1000175-Shapira2">[76]</xref>
###xml 269 293 269 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rrf-3(pk1426);glp-4(bn2)</italic>
###xml 298 310 298 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pha-1(e2123)</italic>
###xml 338 351 332 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-7(tm1907)</italic>
###xml 353 367 347 361 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ins-11(tm1053)</italic>
###xml 431 439 425 433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">cdc-25.1</italic>
###xml 1210 1219 1170 1179 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s012">Tables S1</xref>
###xml 1221 1223 1181 1183 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s014">S3</xref>
###xml 1229 1231 1189 1191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="ppat.1000175.s015">S4</xref>
###xml 35 45 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
###xml 57 61 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 643 647 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 854 858 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Assays to determine the ability of C. elegans to survive PA14 infection were performed as described [76]. Briefly, to avoid the confounding effects of progeny production and internal hatching on survival, sterile worms were used in survival assays. To sterilize worms, rrf-3(pk1426);glp-4(bn2) and pha-1(e2123) were raised at 25degreesC. ins-7(tm1907), ins-11(tm1053), and wildtype controls were sterilized using RNAi knockdown of cdc-25.1. VP303 and NR222 worms are resistant to RNAi in the germline. Thus, VP303, NR222 and N2 worms were grown at 20degreesC and shifted to 27.5degreesC for 24 hours at the L3/L4 molt, which causes sterility. PA14 was grown overnight in King's Broth containing 100 mg/ml rifampicin at 37degreesC. 10 microl was spread on modified NGM and grown for 24 hours at 37degreesC. Worms were infected at 25degreesC by feeding on PA14 lawns. Kaplan-Meier survival analysis was performed using StatView 5.0.1. The Mantel-Cox logrank test was used to assess statistical significance of differences in survival. Only p-values<0.01 were considered significant. Mean time to death and standard error of the mean was calculated in StatView and then normalized to N2 for graphical comparison (Tables S1, S3, and S4).
###end p 89

Knockdown of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 by RNAi enhances the susceptibility of C. elegans to P. aeruginosa infection. ###begin p 100
###xml 5 18 5 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P. aeruginosa</italic>
###xml 80 90 80 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 136 141 136 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 146 151 146 151 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">spp-1</italic>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pscD</italic>
###xml 472 477 472 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7</italic>
###xml 542 546 542 546 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">gacA</italic>
###xml 548 552 548 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lasR</italic>
###xml 554 558 554 558 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">rhlR</italic>

###xml 578 582 578 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pscD</italic>
###xml 596 600 596 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dsbA</italic>
###xml 602 606 602 606 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pqsA</italic>
###xml 684 694 684 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lys-7::GFP</italic>

Many P. aeruginosa virulence factors are not required for immune suppression in C. elegans. (A) Expression of the host defense effector lys-7 and spp-1 in wildtype worms exposed to wildtype PA14 and the PA14 mutant pscD and PA14_41070 measured by qRT-PCR. Mean transcript levels are plotted relative to matched controls exposed to OP50-1. Error bars indicated SEM. 3 replicates of each condition were examined. * t-test, p<0.05 (B) Expression of the host defense effector lys-7 in wildtype worms exposed to wildtype PA14 and the PA14 mutants gacA, lasR, rhlR, exoU, exoT, exoY, pscD, PA14_41070, dsbA, pqsA, PA14_23420, PA14_23430, and PA14_59010 measured by visual classification of lys-7::GFP fluorescence as high or low intensity at 100x total magnification. Expression of lys-7::GFP in uninfected worms was the standard for high intensity fluorescence. Data is also shown in Table S1. * t-test, p<0.05 (C-D) Fluorescence micrographs of lys-7::GFP worms categorized as (C) high or (D) low expression.

###xml 113 126 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 192 205 <span type="species:ncbi:287">P. aeruginosa</span>
###xml 495 499 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 527 531 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
Knockdown of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 by RNAi decreases the resistance of daf-2(e1370) mutants to colonization by P. aeruginosa. RNAi knockdown of thn-2, lys-7, and spp-1 resulted in increased P. aeruginosa accumulation in daf-2(e1370) worms compared to control RNAi (Fisher's exact test; p = 0.0035, p = 0.0054, and p<0.0001, respectively). RNAi knockdown of sod-3 did not significantly affect colonization (Fisher's exact test, p>0.9999). RNAi or control treated daf-2(e1370) were exposed to a PA14 strain that expresses GFP (PA14-GFP) as young adults for 108 hr. Individual worms were classified as having detectable or undetectable GFP fluorescence in the intestinal lumen by visual inspection at 200x total magnification. For each RNAi treatment, a total of 65 worms were assayed blind.

The expression of gst-4 is repressed in worms exposed to P. aeruginosa in a skn-1-independent manner. (A) Fluorescence intensity of gst-4::GFP in worms exposed to wildtype PA14 and the PA14 mutants gacA, lasR and rhlR. Worms of uniformly bright GFP intensity were placed on PA14 for 24 hours. Individual worms were scored for GFP intensity in three categories: low, medium, and high. Population proportions are significantly different in all pairwise comparisons with the exception of lasR and rhlR, which are statistically indistinguishable (Chi-square test, p<0.05). (B) Expression of gst-4 measured in N2, daf-2(e1370), daf-16(mu86), and daf-16(mu86);daf-2(e1370) exposed to OP50-1 and PA14. Mean transcript levels were plotted relative to N2 OP50-1. Error bars represent SEM. t-test ˆ p<0.05 comparison to N2 PA14, + p<0.05 comparing OP50-1 to PA14. (C) Mean (and SEM) of log2 scale transcript levels relative to N2 OP50-1 for gst-4 in skn-1 RNAi and vector control worms exposed to OP50-1 and PA14.

###xml 138 142 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
###xml 217 221 <span type="species:ncbi:287">PA14</span>
ins-7 but not ins-11 is required for resistance to P. aeruginosa. Survival of N2, ins-7(tm1907) and ins-11(tm1053) worms was monitored on PA14 over time at 25degreesC. ins-7(tm1907) is significantly more resistant to PA14 than N2 or ins-11(tm1053) (logrank, p<0.0001 and p = 0.0002, respectively). ins-11(tm1053) is statistically indistinguishable from N2 (logrank, p = 0.0902).
